The Second Argument: Division as Destruction and Creation
Al-Jurjani presents the second argument that division entails destruction and creation and responds to the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the second kalam argument for atomism and its rebuttal of the continuity assumption.

Core Idea
Dividing a true continuum would destroy and recreate — an absurdity.

The mutakallimun argued that bodies cannot be truly continuous because dividing a continuum would entail destroying the original and creating two new entities. This passage presents that argument, explains its reasoning, shows its absurd consequence, and answers an objection. Pay close attention to the logical flow: conditional, implication, proof, and counterexample.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the conditional structure: 'If X, then Y.' Identify the main claim and its consequence.
The key conditional is: if divisible were one continuous, then division = annihilation + creation.
2
Understand the implication
Why does division of a continuum necessarily mean annihilation? Because a single continuous essence cannot become two separate essences without ceasing to be what it was.
The proof uses the impossibility of a thing being both one and two at different times without transformation.
3
Examine the absurd consequence
The author then shows that if division were annihilation and creation, even splitting the ocean with a mosquito's needle would destroy the ocean — clearly false to reason.
This is a reductio ad absurdum to reject the consequent.
4
Consider the objection and its answer
The objection claims that this is just an improbability, not a logical impossibility. The answer: in such disputes, claiming necessity is not accepted.
The response shows that the argument is not refuted by mere improbability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه ( الثاني : لو كان القابل للانقسام واحدا في نفسه متصلا في حد ذاته ( كان التفريق ( الوارد على ذلك القابل ( إعداما له ) وإيجادا متصلة لغيره ) والتالي باطل أما الملازمة فلأن التفريق حينئذ إعدام لهوية ) هي حد ذاتها ( وإحداث لهويتين منفصلتين لم تكونا موجودتين في تلك الهوية الاتصالية وإلا كانت منقسمة بالفعل والمفروض خلافه. وقد وجب كون التفريق على ذلك التقدير إعداماً وإحداثاً ( فإن من المحال أن الشيء المعين يكون تارة هوية واحدة لا انفصال فيها أصلاً ) وتارة هويتين متفاصلتين . ( وأما بطلان اللازم فلانه ) أي اللازم ( يوجب أن يكون شق البعوض بإبرته للبحر المحيط إعداماً لذلك البحر وإيجاداً لبحرين آخرين وبديهة العقل تنفيه ) . وقد أجيب عنه : بأنه استبعاد لا يفيد اليقين ودعوى الضرورة في محل الخلاف غير مسموعة .
The second aspect: If what is divisible were one in itself and continuous in its essence, then the division applied to that divisible would be an annihilation of it and a creation of something else continuous with it. The consequent is false. As for the implication, it is because the division then is an annihilation of an essence (which is its essence) and a bringing-into-existence of two separate essences that did not exist in that continuous essence, otherwise it would be actually divided, contrary to assumption. And it must be that the division on that assumption is annihilation and creation (for it is impossible that a specific thing is sometimes a single essence with no separation at all and at other times two separate essences). As for the falsity of the necessary consequence, it is because it (i.e., the consequence) requires that splitting the ocean with a mosquito's needle be an annihilation of that ocean and a creation of two other oceans, and the intuition of the intellect rejects it. And it was answered: that it is an improbability which does not yield certainty, and the claim of necessity in a point of disagreement is not accepted.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument (al-wajh al-thani) of the mutakallimun for the composition of bodies from atoms. The argument begins with a conditional: if the divisible were one in itself and continuous in its essence, then dividing it would be an annihilation of that single continuous entity and a creation of something else in its place. The reasoning is that division of a true continuum cannot be mere separation of pre-existing parts; it must destroy the original identity and create two new ones, since otherwise the original would have been actually divided already. The consequent (that division is annihilation and creation) is claimed false, and the author proves the implication (mulazama) by explaining that division under this assumption annihilates the original essence and creates two new ones that were not present in the continuous essence. Then he states the falsity of the necessary consequence (lazim): if this were true, then splitting the ocean with a mosquito's needle would annihilate the ocean and create two new oceans, which is absurd to reason. The objection is answered by saying that this is merely an improbability (istib'aad) rather than a certain proof, and that claiming intuitive necessity in this disputed matter is not admissible.

Key Terms
الوجه الثاني
التفريق
إعدام
إيجاد
الهوية الاتصالية
استبعاد
بديهة العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument denies the possibility of any division in bodies.
Correction: The argument denies that division can occur in a truly continuous whole; it actually shows that bodies must be composed of discrete parts (atoms) that can be separated without annihilation.

Checkpoint
According to the second argument, what would dividing a truly continuous body necessarily entail?
A) Separation of pre-existing parts
B) Annihilation of the original body and creation of two new bodies
C) Change in the body's color
D) Nothing, it is a simple process

Key Takeaway
The second argument shows that the assumption of a true continuum leads to absurdity, supporting the belief that bodies are composed of indivisible atoms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the argument shows that assuming things are truly continuous leads to absurdity in division, how does that challenge your own assumptions about the nature of reality? Are there areas in your life where you assume things are fixed and continuous, but actually they are composed of discrete moments or parts — and what does that mean for how you live?
?
The argument uses a logical reductio to show that even a tiny division would annihilate and recreate the whole. This highlights the gravity of assuming continuity. How does this affect your view of God's constant creation and annihilation of every atom at every moment? Do you live with the awareness that your very existence is being continually recreated?
?
The objection says this is just an improbability. The author replies that in such a matter, claiming necessity is not accepted. When you face points of disagreement in your faith, do you dismiss arguments as 'just improbable' without engaging with their logical structure? How can you cultivate intellectual humility while still holding firm to truth?

The First Proof Against Infinite Actual Parts
Al-Jurjani presents the first proof and its illustration with the swift and slow.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the first proof that a finite body cannot be composed of infinite actual parts, and why the impossibility of traversing a finite distance in finite time would follow if it were.

Core Idea
If a finite distance had infinite actual parts, you could never cross it—but you can.

The first proof against infinite actual parts in a body takes the form of a reductio ad absurdum. It begins by assuming the opposite—that a finite distance is made of infinite actual parts—and then derives an impossible consequence: that crossing that distance would require infinite time. Since we observe traversal in finite time, the original assumption must be false. This lesson unpacks that argument and the example of the swift and the slow that illustrates it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the logical structure: if...then...but...therefore.
2
Identify the antecedent and consequent
The antecedent is the claim that a finite distance is composed of infinite actual parts. The consequent is that it cannot be traversed in finite time. The proof shows the consequent is false, so the antecedent is false.
3
Understand the swift and slow example
The example of a swift runner not overtaking a slow one over a short distance illustrates the absurdity: if the distance has infinite parts, even the swift cannot cover it in finite time, so he never catches up. But we know that in reality he does.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The falsity of the consequent (impossible traversal) proves the falsity of the antecedent (infinite actual parts). This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نصف نصفها وهكذا إلى ما لا نهاية له فامتنع قطعها إلا في زمان غير متناه. (ولم يلحق السريع البطيء) إذا توسط بينهما مسافة قليلة فإن تلك المسافة مركبة من أجزاء غير متناهية لا يمكن للسريع قطعها في زمان متناه فلا يلحق البطيء قطعاً، ( وبطلان اللازم وهو امتناع قطع المسافة المتناهية في زمان متناه وعدم لحوق السريع للبطيء ( دليل بطلان الملزوم) وهو كون تلك المسافة مركبة من أجزاء موجودة بالفعل غير متناهية . ويحكى أن العلاف لما أورد هذا الإلزام على النظام التجأ إلى القول بالطفرة فقال : إن المتحرك قد يقطع المسافة بأن يحاذي بعض أجزائها دون بعض ولا حاجة له إلى هذه المكابرة بل يكفيه أن يقول : كما أن المسافة المتناهية مركبة من أجزاء موجودة غير متناهية كذلك الزمان المتناهي مشتمل على أجزاء غير متناهية فيتقابل أجزاء المسافة والزمان معاً فيمكن قطعها فيه واعلم أن النظام لم يكن قائلاً بالجزء الذي لا يتجزأ وتركب الجسم منه إلا أنه لزمه ذلك من حيث لا يدري فإنه لما وقف قوله : ( وقد أجيب : بأنه استبعاد إلخ والتحقيق أنه إن أريد الجزء المانع للاتصال فلا شك في انعدامه كما إذا كان التركيب من الأجزاء بالفعل وإن أريد بالجزء المانع التركيب وإن أريد الاتصال والتفريق فقوله وأجيب ، إلخ، أي لا نسلم أن المقاطع نفس الماء فهو يجتمع مع متمايزة في الخارج، بل تمايزها في الذهن بعد فرض القسمة . قوله : (وهو) كون تلك المسافة إلخ ) فإن قيل : بطلان اللازم المذكور إنما يستلزم بطلان تركب المسافة من أجزاء غير متناهية وكل مسافة متركبة من أجزاء غير متناهية . قلت : تناهي الأجزاء في الامتدادات الثلاثة يستلزم تناهي الشكل بناء على أن الأجزاء التي وسط المسافة المتناهية للأجزاء التي في الامتدادات الثلاثة المتصلة بعضها ببعض لايزيد عليها في العدد أنه لا يجوز أن يتصل بجزء واحد جزءان أو نقول : المراد كون المسافة من حيث هي مسافة أي من حيث وقع فيها الحركة متناهية والنظام يقول بعدم التناهي بالفعل في كل امتدادات غير متناهية إذ لو تناهت في امتداد بناء على أن جميع الانقسامات الممكنة عنده حاصلة بالفعل والانقسامات في كل امتداد غير متناهية إذ لو تناهت في امتداد لزم الجزء وما في حكمه . قوله : ( ولا حاجة له أي للنظام إلى هذه المكابرة وهي القول بالطفرة ومما يدل على كونه مكابرة إنما هذا القلم فيحصل خط السواد من غير أن يبقى في خلاله أجزاء بيض وليس كذلك وذلك لأن المقصود هاهنا هو إيراد لازم آخر باطل . فلو قال : لم يلحق المتحرك الساكن لكان هذا اللازم مندرجاً في اللازم الأول فلم يحصل المقصود هذا خلف . قوله : ( كذلك الزمان المتناهي مشتمل على أجزاء غير متناهية هذا مع القول بتناهي الآنات المتجددة مكابرة أيضاً فإن بداهة العقل يقتضي عدم تناهي الزمان المركب من الغير المتناهية المتتالية في التحقيق كما لا يخفى . الآنات على أدلة نفاة الجزء ولم يقدر على ردها أذعن لها وحكم بأن الجسم انقسامات لا تتناهى، لكنه لم يفرق بين ما هو موجود في الشيء بالقوة وبين ما هو موجود فيه بالفعل، فظن أن الانقسامات التي لا تتناهى حاصلة في الجسم بالفعل، فصرح بأن في الجسم أجزاء غير متناهية موجودة بالفعل ولزمه القول بالجزء، فإنه إذا كان كل انقسام ممكن في الجسم حاصلاً فيه بالفعل فما لا يكون من الانقسامات حاصلاً في الجسم امتنع حصوله فيه، فتكون أجزاؤه غير قابلة للانقسام، فقد وقع فيما كان هارباً عنه نافياً له غير معترف به، ومن ثمة نقل عنه أنه لما عيره مثبتو الجزء على القول بالطفرة، أجاب : بأنها ليست أبعد مما لزمكم من القول بتفكك الرحى فالتزمتموه .
Half of half of it, and so on to infinity, so cutting it is impossible except in infinite time. (And the swift does not overtake the slow) if a small distance intervenes between them, for that distance is composed of infinite parts that the swift cannot traverse in finite time, so he absolutely does not overtake the slow. (And the falsity of the consequent – namely, the impossibility of traversing a finite distance in finite time and the non-overtaking of the swift of the slow – is evidence for the falsity of the antecedent), which is that that distance is composed of actually existing infinite parts. It is narrated that when al-‘Allāf presented this objection to al-Naẓẓām, he resorted to the doctrine of ṭafra (leap) and said: The mover may traverse the distance by aligning with some of its parts without others, and he has no need for this arrogance; rather, it suffices him to say: Just as a finite distance is composed of existing infinite parts, so also finite time contains infinite parts, so the parts of distance and time correspond together, and thus it can be traversed in it. And know that al-Naẓẓām was not an adherent of the indivisible part (al-juz’ alladhī lā yatajazza’) and that the body is composed of it, but rather that adhered to him without his knowledge, because when he stopped... His saying: (And it was answered: it is an improbability, etc.) And the verification is that if what is meant by part is that which prevents continuity, there is no doubt of its non-existence, as when composition is from actual parts; and if what is meant by part is that which prevents composition... And his saying: (and if continuity and separation are meant) then his saying: and it was answered, etc., i.e., we do not concede that the sections are the same water, for it combines with distinctness in the external, rather their distinctness is in the mind after assuming division. His saying: (and it) meaning that distance, etc.) For if it is said: the falsity of the mentioned consequent only entails the falsity of the composition of the distance from infinite parts, and every distance is composed of infinite parts. I say: the finitude of parts in the three dimensions entails the finitude of the shape, based on the fact that the parts in the middle of the finite distance do not exceed in number the parts in the three dimensions connected to each other, and it is not permissible for two parts to be connected to one part. Or we say: what is meant is that the distance insofar as it is distance, i.e., insofar as motion occurs in it, is finite, and al-Naẓẓām affirms actual infinity in all dimensions, because if it were finite in a dimension, then all possible divisions according to him are actually realized, and divisions in every dimension are infinite, so if they are finite in a dimension, the part and what is like it would follow. His saying: (And he has no need – i.e., al-Naẓẓām – for this arrogance, which is the doctrine of ṭafra) and what indicates its being arrogance is that this pen produces a black line without leaving white parts in between, and it is not so. And because the purpose here is to present another false consequent. So if he had said: the mover does not overtake the stationary, this consequent would be included in the first consequent, so the purpose would not be achieved; this is a contradiction. His saying: (Similarly, finite time contains infinite parts) this, together with the doctrine of finite instants, is also arrogance, for the intuition of the intellect necessitates the infinity of time composed of successive infinites in reality, as is not hidden. The instants. On the proofs of the negators of the part, and he was unable to refute them, so he acquiesced to them and judged that the body has divisions that do not end. But he did not distinguish between what exists in a thing potentially and what exists in it actually, so he thought that the infinite divisions are actually realized in the body, so he declared that in the body there are actually existing infinite parts, and the doctrine of the part adhered to him. For if every possible division in the body is actually realized in it, then what is not among the divisions realized in the body is impossible to occur in it, so its parts are indivisible. Thus he fell into that which he was fleeing from, denying it, not acknowledging it. And hence it is narrated that when the proponents of the part taunted him about his doctrine of ṭafra, he replied: It is not more remote than what adhered to you from the doctrine of the disintegration of the millstone, so you accepted it.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof that a body cannot be composed of infinite actual parts. The argument begins with a reductio: if a finite distance is composed of infinite actual parts, then traversing it would take infinite time, but we observe traversal in finite time. The example of a swift runner not overtaking a slow one over a short distance illustrates this, since the distance is composed of infinite parts uncrossable in finite time. The falsity of this impossible consequence proves the falsity of the antecedent—that distance has infinite actual parts. The passage then narrates that when al-‘Allāf pressed this objection on al-Naẓẓām, al-Naẓẓām resorted to the doctrine of ṭafra (leap), claiming that a mover can skip parts. However, the commentary dismisses this as arrogance, noting that a finite penstroke does not skip white parts. Al-Naẓẓām’s own position is analyzed: he denied the indivisible part but, under pressure from arguments against atomists, accepted infinite divisions actually in the body, thus inadvertently falling into atomism. The passage ends with a report of al-Naẓẓām’s retort to his critics, comparing their view to a millstone’s disintegration.

Key Terms
أجزاء غير متناهية
ملزوم
لازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the proof denies infinite divisibility altogether, but it only denies that the parts exist actually in a finite body.
Correction: The proof targets actual infinite parts, not potential divisibility, which does not preclude traversal.

Checkpoint
What does the first proof conclude must be false?
A) That a finite distance is composed of infinite actual parts.
B) That a finite distance is composed of finite potential parts.
C) That time is composed of infinite parts.
D) That motion is possible.

Key Takeaway
The first proof shows that a finite body cannot contain actually infinite parts because that would make traversal impossible, which contradicts everyday experience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You cross a room every day. This proof shows that the very possibility of your walking is evidence that the world is not composed of infinite parts. How does this affect your certainty that the world is created with finite limits? What does that imply about the Creator's power and wisdom, and how should that change the way you move through your daily life with awareness of Him?
?
The swift overtakes the slow—a simple, everyday observation that disproves a major philosophical misconception. What seemingly trivial observations in your life might be hiding profound truths about Allah? Are you paying attention to them, or do you dismiss them as ordinary? Make a commitment to notice one such sign today and reflect on it.
?
If this proof is sound, then every finite body must have a finite number of actual parts. Your own body is a finite body. What does that say about its origin? Does it force you to consider that it was brought into existence by a Creator? If so, how does that reshape your sense of accountability to that Creator for how you use your body and time?

Al-Naẓẓām's Dilemma and the Doctrine of Ṭafra
Al-Jurjani narrates al-Naẓẓām's dilemma and the critique of ṭafra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Naẓẓām's response to the first proof—the doctrine of ṭafra (leap)—and how his position on infinite divisions led him inadvertently into atomism.

Core Idea
To avoid infinite parts, al-Naẓẓām invented the leap—but fell into the very trap he was fleeing.

After presenting the first proof, the text turns to a historical episode. When al-‘Allāf pressed this objection on al-Naẓẓām, al-Naẓẓām countered with the idea of a 'leap' (ṭafra), claiming that a mover can skip over parts. The commentary dismisses this as arrogance and goes on to analyze al-Naẓẓām's own position, showing that he inadvertently fell into the belief in indivisible parts that he had rejected. This lesson explores that debate and the crucial distinction between potential and actual infinity.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative about al-Naẓẓām's response
The passage recounts that al-Naẓẓām resorted to the doctrine of ṭafra when confronted with the proof.
2
Understand the ṭafra doctrine and its refutation
Ṭafra claims that a mover can traverse a distance by aligning with some parts and skipping others. The commentary refutes this by the example of a pen: it cannot skip white parts in a continuous stroke.
3
Analyze al-Naẓẓām's inconsistency
Al-Naẓẓām denied the indivisible part but, under pressure from arguments against atomists, accepted that the body has actually infinite divisions. This led him to the very conclusion he opposed: that there must be indivisible parts.
4
Reflect on the lesson
This episode teaches the importance of distinguishing potential from actual infinity in theological arguments.

Source Text

(ولم يلحق السريع البطيء) إذا توسط بينهما مسافة قليلة فإن تلك المسافة مركبة من أجزاء غير متناهية لا يمكن للسريع قطعها في زمان متناه فلا يلحق البطيء قطعاً، ( وبطلان اللازم وهو امتناع قطع المسافة المتناهية في زمان متناه وعدم لحوق السريع للبطيء ( دليل بطلان الملزوم) وهو كون تلك المسافة مركبة من أجزاء موجودة بالفعل غير متناهية . ويحكى أن العلاف لما أورد هذا الإلزام على النظام التجأ إلى القول بالطفرة فقال : إن المتحرك قد يقطع المسافة بأن يحاذي بعض أجزائها دون بعض ولا حاجة له إلى هذه المكابرة بل يكفيه أن يقول : كما أن المسافة المتناهية مركبة من أجزاء موجودة غير متناهية كذلك الزمان المتناهي مشتمل على أجزاء غير متناهية فيتقابل أجزاء المسافة والزمان معاً فيمكن قطعها فيه واعلم أن النظام لم يكن قائلاً بالجزء الذي لا يتجزأ وتركب الجسم منه إلا أنه لزمه ذلك من حيث لا يدري فإنه لما وقف قوله : ( وقد أجيب : بأنه استبعاد إلخ والتحقيق أنه إن أريد الجزء المانع للاتصال فلا شك في انعدامه كما إذا كان التركيب من الأجزاء بالفعل وإن أريد بالجزء المانع التركيب وإن أريد الاتصال والتفريق فقوله وأجيب ، إلخ، أي لا نسلم أن المقاطع نفس الماء فهو يجتمع مع متمايزة في الخارج، بل تمايزها في الذهن بعد فرض القسمة . قوله : (وهو) كون تلك المسافة إلخ ) فإن قيل : بطلان اللازم المذكور إنما يستلزم بطلان تركب المسافة من أجزاء غير متناهية وكل مسافة متركبة من أجزاء غير متناهية . قلت : تناهي الأجزاء في الامتدادات الثلاثة يستلزم تناهي الشكل بناء على أن الأجزاء التي وسط المسافة المتناهية للأجزاء التي في الامتدادات الثلاثة المتصلة بعضها ببعض لايزيد عليها في العدد أنه لا يجوز أن يتصل بجزء واحد جزءان أو نقول : المراد كون المسافة من حيث هي مسافة أي من حيث وقع فيها الحركة متناهية والنظام يقول بعدم التناهي بالفعل في كل امتدادات غير متناهية إذ لو تناهت في امتداد بناء على أن جميع الانقسامات الممكنة عنده حاصلة بالفعل والانقسامات في كل امتداد غير متناهية إذ لو تناهت في امتداد لزم الجزء وما في حكمه . قوله : ( ولا حاجة له أي للنظام إلى هذه المكابرة وهي القول بالطفرة ومما يدل على كونه مكابرة إنما هذا القلم فيحصل خط السواد من غير أن يبقى في خلاله أجزاء بيض وليس كذلك وذلك لأن المقصود هاهنا هو إيراد لازم آخر باطل . فلو قال : لم يلحق المتحرك الساكن لكان هذا اللازم مندرجاً في اللازم الأول فلم يحصل المقصود هذا خلف . قوله : ( كذلك الزمان المتناهي مشتمل على أجزاء غير متناهية هذا مع القول بتناهي الآنات المتجددة مكابرة أيضاً فإن بداهة العقل يقتضي عدم تناهي الزمان المركب من الغير المتناهية المتتالية في التحقيق كما لا يخفى . الآنات على أدلة نفاة الجزء ولم يقدر على ردها أذعن لها وحكم بأن الجسم انقسامات لا تتناهى، لكنه لم يفرق بين ما هو موجود في الشيء بالقوة وبين ما هو موجود فيه بالفعل، فظن أن الانقسامات التي لا تتناهى حاصلة في الجسم بالفعل، فصرح بأن في الجسم أجزاء غير متناهية موجودة بالفعل ولزمه القول بالجزء، فإنه إذا كان كل انقسام ممكن في الجسم حاصلاً فيه بالفعل فما لا يكون من الانقسامات حاصلاً في الجسم امتنع حصوله فيه، فتكون أجزاؤه غير قابلة للانقسام، فقد وقع فيما كان هارباً عنه نافياً له غير معترف به، ومن ثمة نقل عنه أنه لما عيره مثبتو الجزء على القول بالطفرة، أجاب : بأنها ليست أبعد مما لزمكم من القول بتفكك الرحى فالتزمتموه .
Half of half of it, and so on to infinity, so cutting it is impossible except in infinite time. (And the swift does not overtake the slow) if a small distance intervenes between them, for that distance is composed of infinite parts that the swift cannot traverse in finite time, so he absolutely does not overtake the slow. (And the falsity of the consequent – namely, the impossibility of traversing a finite distance in finite time and the non-overtaking of the swift of the slow – is evidence for the falsity of the antecedent), which is that that distance is composed of actually existing infinite parts. It is narrated that when al-‘Allāf presented this objection to al-Naẓẓām, he resorted to the doctrine of ṭafra (leap) and said: The mover may traverse the distance by aligning with some of its parts without others, and he has no need for this arrogance; rather, it suffices him to say: Just as a finite distance is composed of existing infinite parts, so also finite time contains infinite parts, so the parts of distance and time correspond together, and thus it can be traversed in it. And know that al-Naẓẓām was not an adherent of the indivisible part (al-juz’ alladhī lā yatajazza’) and that the body is composed of it, but rather that adhered to him without his knowledge, because when he stopped... His saying: (And it was answered: it is an improbability, etc.) And the verification is that if what is meant by part is that which prevents continuity, there is no doubt of its non-existence, as when composition is from actual parts; and if what is meant by part is that which prevents composition... And his saying: (and if continuity and separation are meant) then his saying: and it was answered, etc., i.e., we do not concede that the sections are the same water, for it combines with distinctness in the external, rather their distinctness is in the mind after assuming division. His saying: (and it) meaning that distance, etc.) For if it is said: the falsity of the mentioned consequent only entails the falsity of the composition of the distance from infinite parts, and every distance is composed of infinite parts. I say: the finitude of parts in the three dimensions entails the finitude of the shape, based on the fact that the parts in the middle of the finite distance do not exceed in number the parts in the three dimensions connected to each other, and it is not permissible for two parts to be connected to one part. Or we say: what is meant is that the distance insofar as it is distance, i.e., insofar as motion occurs in it, is finite, and al-Naẓẓām affirms actual infinity in all dimensions, because if it were finite in a dimension, then all possible divisions according to him are actually realized, and divisions in every dimension are infinite, so if they are finite in a dimension, the part and what is like it would follow. His saying: (And he has no need – i.e., al-Naẓẓām – for this arrogance, which is the doctrine of ṭafra) and what indicates its being arrogance is that this pen produces a black line without leaving white parts in between, and it is not so. And because the purpose here is to present another false consequent. So if he had said: the mover does not overtake the stationary, this consequent would be included in the first consequent, so the purpose would not be achieved; this is a contradiction. His saying: (Similarly, finite time contains infinite parts) this, together with the doctrine of finite instants, is also arrogance, for the intuition of the intellect necessitates the infinity of time composed of successive infinites in reality, as is not hidden. The instants. On the proofs of the negators of the part, and he was unable to refute them, so he acquiesced to them and judged that the body has divisions that do not end. But he did not distinguish between what exists in a thing potentially and what exists in it actually, so he thought that the infinite divisions are actually realized in the body, so he declared that in the body there are actually existing infinite parts, and the doctrine of the part adhered to him. For if every possible division in the body is actually realized in it, then what is not among the divisions realized in the body is impossible to occur in it, so its parts are indivisible. Thus he fell into that which he was fleeing from, denying it, not acknowledging it. And hence it is narrated that when the proponents of the part taunted him about his doctrine of ṭafra, he replied: It is not more remote than what adhered to you from the doctrine of the disintegration of the millstone, so you accepted it.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof that a body cannot be composed of infinite actual parts. The argument begins with a reductio: if a finite distance is composed of infinite actual parts, then traversing it would take infinite time, but we observe traversal in finite time. The example of a swift runner not overtaking a slow one over a short distance illustrates this, since the distance is composed of infinite parts uncrossable in finite time. The falsity of this impossible consequence proves the falsity of the antecedent—that distance has infinite actual parts. The passage then narrates that when al-‘Allāf pressed this objection on al-Naẓẓām, al-Naẓẓām resorted to the doctrine of ṭafra (leap), claiming that a mover can skip parts. However, the commentary dismisses this as arrogance, noting that a finite penstroke does not skip white parts. Al-Naẓẓām’s own position is analyzed: he denied the indivisible part but, under pressure from arguments against atomists, accepted infinite divisions actually in the body, thus inadvertently falling into atomism. The passage ends with a report of al-Naẓẓām’s retort to his critics, comparing their view to a millstone’s disintegration.

Key Terms
طفرة
جزء لا يتجزأ
مكابرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that al-Naẓẓām's ṭafra is a viable reply, but it fails because motion is continuous and skipping parts contradicts observable continuity.
Correction: The pen example shows continuity is preserved in motion, so skipping is false.

Checkpoint
What was al-Naẓẓām's main error according to the commentary?
A) He denied the indivisible part.
B) He conflated potential and actual divisions.
C) He accepted the first proof.
D) He rejected motion.

Key Takeaway
Al-Naẓẓām's attempt to avoid atomism by accepting actual infinite divisions only led him to atomism, highlighting the importance of distinguishing potential from actual infinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you insisted on a solution that only created a bigger problem, like al-Naẓẓām's leap? How can you recognize when your reasoning, like his, is marked by mukābara—arrogant stubbornness—rather than humble submission to truth? What concrete step will you take this week to examine a belief or habit you hold tightly, even if it might be contradictory?
?
Al-Naẓẓām fell into what he was fleeing because he didn't distinguish between potential and actual. In your spiritual life, where are you confusing what could be (potential) with what actually is (actual) regarding your faith, your sins, or your relationship with Allah? How does this confusion prevent you from repenting or growing? Commit now to one specific area where you will stop deceiving yourself and face the truth.
?
The passage ends with al-Naẓẓām accusing his critics of an equal absurdity rather than admitting his error. When have you done the same—deflected criticism by pointing out faults in others instead of humbly accepting correction? How does your pride affect your pursuit of truth? Will you today ask Allah to grant you the humility to admit when you are wrong, even if it feels like losing face?

Why a Finite Body Cannot Have Infinite Parts
Al-Jurjani argues that a finite body cannot contain infinite parts between its limits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a finite body cannot contain an infinite number of actual parts, based on the principle that the infinite cannot be enclosed between finite boundaries.

Core Idea
The infinite cannot be confined — a finite body must have finite parts.

Al-Jurjani now presents his second proof against the existence of infinite actual parts in a body. By reflecting on the finite boundaries of any physical object, he shows that infinite parts are logically impossible. This passage uses a simple spatial argument that appeals to basic intuition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
The body under discussion is finite in volume and magnitude, so it is enclosed between its two surrounding ends (its boundaries). Its parts are likewise enclosed between these same boundaries.
We are dealing with actual parts, not potential divisions.
2
Apply the impossibility principle
It is impossible for an infinite number of things to be enclosed between two finite boundaries. Since the parts are enclosed, they cannot be infinite.
This is a self-evident rational principle.
3
Consider the exception
The only way to avoid the conclusion is to claim that the parts interpenetrate (overlap in space), so that an infinite number could fit without exceeding the boundaries.
Interpenetration means multiple objects occupy the same space.
4
See why the exception fails
Immediate intuition (badīha) testifies that interpenetration is false. We directly know that two bodies cannot occupy the same space.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه (الثاني: أنه أي الجسم الذي نحن بصدده متناه بالحجم والمقدار فهو محصور بين الطرفين المحيطين به وكذا أجزاؤه محصورة بينهما، ( وانحصار ما لا يتناهى بين الحاصرين محال فاستحال أن تكون أجزاؤه الموجودة فيه بالفعل غير متناهية إلا أن يلتزم التداخل فيما بين تلك الأجزاء لكنه مما تشهد البديهة ببطلانه.
The second proof: that (i.e., the body we are dealing with) is finite in volume and magnitude, so it is enclosed between its two surrounding ends, and likewise its parts are enclosed between them. (And the enclosure of what is infinite between enclosers is impossible). So it is impossible for its actually existing parts to be infinite, unless one commits to interpenetration among those parts, but intuition testifies to its falsity.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage gives the second proof against infinite actual parts in a body. The body under discussion is finite in size, bounded by two limits (e.g., its surface boundaries). Its parts are likewise enclosed between these limits. But it is impossible for something infinite to be enclosed between two finite boundaries. Therefore, the actual parts of a finite body cannot be infinite. The only escape would be to claim that the parts interpenetrate (i.e., overlap in space), but immediate intuition (badīha) declares this impossible. Thus the conclusion holds.

Key Terms
متناه
محصور
التداخل
البديهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof claims that a body cannot be divided infinitely (potential infinity).
Correction: The proof does not deny potential infinite divisibility; it denies that actual infinite parts exist in a finite substance. The body can be divided without end potentially, but at any moment it contains only finite actual parts.

Checkpoint
What does the second proof say must be the case for the body's parts?
A) They are infinite in number.
B) They are finite in number.
C) They are interpenetrating.
D) They are indivisible.

Key Takeaway
A finite body must have a finite number of actual parts because the infinite cannot be contained within finite boundaries.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
A finite body cannot contain infinite parts. Your life is finite, yet you try to pack it with infinite attachments and distractions. What 'parts' must you remove to stop living against reality?
?
Interpenetration is false by intuition, yet you might allow contradictions in your faith—loving the world and Allah, or claiming to submit while obeying your own desires. Where are you forcing interpenetration in your soul?
?
Since the parts are finite and enclosed, what does your finite capacity for worship require you to prioritize today? Will you choose one sincere act over a thousand distracted ones?

The Third Proof: Composition Must Increase Size
Al-Jurjani proves that composition of parts increases volume, so infinite parts would produce no volume.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof for the finitude of parts, which argues that composition necessarily increases volume, and how it handles the objection of interpenetration.

Core Idea
Composition must increase volume; otherwise infinite parts would yield no size at all.

Al-Jurjani presents a third, more refined argument against infinite parts. He argues that joining parts together must increase the overall volume; otherwise no amount of parts could produce an extended body. This proof confronts the objection that parts might interpenetrate, and shows that even then volume must increase.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse every sentence. Then read the translation to get the full sense of the proof and the subsequent commentary.
Notice that the passage includes not only the main proof but also discussions of objections.
2
Identify the core claim
The core claim is that composition (joining parts) must result in an increase in volume. Underline the statement where this is expressed.
This is the key premise of the proof.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
Consider what would happen if composition did not increase volume: the volume of two parts would equal that of one, and by extension any number of parts (even infinite) would produce no volume. This contradicts the observed extension of bodies.
This forms the backbone of the argument.
4
Examine the objection and reply
The passage addresses the objection that parts could interpenetrate, which might allow no volume increase. Al-Jurjani argues that interpenetration does not help because it still leads to finitude of parts, and if parts are infinite and interpenetrate, volume does increase because there is no 'all' of parts.
This shows the depth of the argument.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Reflect on why this proof supports the finitude of actual parts. The proof shows that composition must increase volume, so a body with extension must have a finite number of parts to produce that volume.
Connect this to the overall goal of proving the existence of indivisible parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه ( الثالث : أن التأليف ) هو ضم بعض الأجزاء الموجودة في الجسم إلى بعض ( لا بد أن يفيد زيادة حجم وإلا لكان حجم الاثنين كحجم الواحد وكذا الثلاثة والأربعة إلى غير النهاية فلا يحصل من تأليف الأجزاء ) وإن كانت غير متناهية (حجم) أصلاً ) والمفروض خلافه ) لأن الجسم له حجم ممتد في الجهات ولا شك أن هذا الحجم لفرط اختلاط الأجزاء البيض في السود بحيث لا امتياز في الحس لأن الأجزاء مصلقون عنها كثيراً، بل لا نسبة لها الأجزاء بالسواد لكونها غير متناهية . قوله : ( ومن ثمة أي ومن أجل أنه غير مقترن بالجزء أجاب بمعنى الجزء بهذا الجواب، فإن قوله : لزمكم يدل على أنه غير مقترن وإلا لزمه أيضاً . قوله : ( وكذا أجزاء إلخ) إن أريد انحصارها مقداراً فمسلم وإن أراد انحصارها عدداً ففيه النزاع . قوله : (إلا) أن يلتزم التداخل لا ينفعه لأنه يلزم تناهي الأجزاء المتناهية في الوضع لأنه يقول : إن جميع الانقسامات الممكنة إلى الأجزاء المقدارية حاصلة بالفعل . قوله : ( مما يشهد إلخ ) أي مداخل له حجم أو مقدار فيما له حجم أو مقدار شبهة البديهة ببطلانه لأنه يستلزم بطلان الحكم البديهي الأولى وهو كون الكل المقداري أعظم من جزئه المقداري . قوله : ( وإن كانت غير متناهية إلخ له أن يقول : قياس غير المتناهي باطل فالأجزاء المتداخلة إذا كانت متناهية لا يفيد التأليف زيادة في الحجم وإذا كانت غير متناهية يفيدها لعدم انقطاع التداخل فلا يمكن أن يقال : جميع الأجزاء المتداخلة ليس حجماً زائداً على حجم الواحد إذ لا جميع.
The third proof: that composition (al-ta’līf) is the joining of some of the parts existing in the body to others; (it must necessarily result in an increase in volume; otherwise, the volume of two would be like the volume of one, and likewise three and four ad infinitum, so no volume would result from the composition of parts) even if they are infinite, (absolutely no volume) (but the contrary is assumed) because the body has a volume extended in dimensions, and there is no doubt that this volume (is due to) the excessive intermixture of white parts in black such that there is no distinction in sensation, because the parts are many [?] and have no proportion to the parts of blackness due to their infinity. His saying: (And from that is...) i.e., because he is not associated with the part, he answered in the sense of the part with this answer, for his saying “it adhered to you” indicates that he is not associated with it, otherwise it would also adhere to him. His saying: (And likewise parts, etc.) if what is meant is their enclosure in magnitude, it is conceded; if what is meant is their enclosure in number, then there is dispute. His saying: (except) that one commits to interpenetration, it does not benefit him, because it entails the finitude of the parts that are finite in position, because he says that all possible divisions into magnitude-parts are actually realized. His saying: (of which intuition testifies, etc.) i.e., that which has volume or magnitude entering into that which has volume or magnitude is intuitively false, because it entails the falsity of the primary intuitive judgment that the quantitative whole is greater than its quantitative part. His saying: (And even if they are infinite, etc.) he can say: analogy of the infinite is invalid, for interpenetrating parts, if finite, composition does not increase volume, but if infinite, it does increase because interpenetration never stops, so one cannot say that all interpenetrating parts do not have a volume exceeding the volume of one, since there is no 'all'.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof that the body's actual parts must be finite. Composition (al-ta’līf) is defined as joining parts together. If composition did not increase volume, then two parts would have the same volume as one, and by extension, any number of parts, even infinite, would yield no volume. But bodies are observed to have extended volume, so composition must increase volume. The passage then includes extensive commentary. The first comment discusses that al-Naẓẓām’s answer about the millstone indicates he is not committed to the indivisible part. The second comment clarifies that 'enclosure of parts' can mean enclosure in magnitude (agreed) or in number (disputed). The third comment deals with interpenetration: even if one accepts interpenetration to avoid the second proof, it does not help, because it would still entail finitude of parts in position. The fourth comment addresses the intuitive judgment that the whole is greater than the part, which interpenetration violates. The final comment argues that infinite parts cannot be treated by analogy with finite parts; if parts interpenetrate and are infinite, they do increase volume because interpenetration is endless, and there is no 'all' to sum.

Key Terms
التأليف
الحجم
التداخل
الكل المقداري
الجزء المقداري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Infinite interpenetrating parts cannot produce any volume increase because interpenetration means no addition.
Correction: Al-Jurjani argues that if parts are infinite and interpenetrate, they do increase volume because interpenetration never stops, so there is no 'all' to sum; thus volume grows without bound.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, what does composition necessarily do?
A) It decreases volume.
B) It increases volume.
C) It has no effect on volume.
D) It makes parts indivisible.

Key Takeaway
The third proof establishes that composition necessarily increases volume, so a body's parts must be finite to produce extended size.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that if composition did not increase volume, even infinite parts would yield no volume. Your life is composed of countless moments—but are they 'composed' in a way that produces a meaningful, increasing nearness to Allah, or are they scattered and cancel each other out, leaving you spiritually empty? What will you do to ensure each action adds real volume to your faith?
?
Al-Jurjani argues that interpenetration does not solve the problem; it only shifts it. Are there 'interpenetrating' excuses in your life—rationalizations that allow you to hold contradictory beliefs or actions? Identify one such area and commit to resolving it according to the truth.
?
The proof concludes that parts must be finite to produce volume. Your time on earth is finite. If every moment is a 'part', how are you composing them to produce a life of weight (volume) before Allah? What one change can you make today to add sincere, lasting volume instead of wasted emptiness?

The Existence of the Point from Touch
Al-Jurjani argues for the existence of the point through the touch of bodies, surfaces, and lines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Jurjani proves the existence of an indivisible point through the necessary chain of touch between bodies, surfaces, and lines.

Core Idea
The point exists because two existents cannot touch by a non-existent.

Al-Jurjani introduces the second type of proof for atoms by focusing on the point. Unlike the first type, this proof does not rely on actual division but on the necessity of touch. By tracing the contact between bodies down to surfaces and lines, he arrives at the point, which is indivisible and serves as a foundation for the atom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow of the argument. Then read the translation to ensure understanding of the logical steps.
Notice that the proof proceeds from bodies to surfaces to lines to points.
2
Identify the chain of touch
Identify the three levels: bodies touch surfaces, surfaces touch lines, lines touch points. Each level implies the existence of the next.
The argument assumes that touch between existents must be by something existent.
3
Understand why the point is indivisible
The point has no dimension; it is a 'something having position' that is not divisible. Reflect on why it cannot be divided.
The point is the extremity of a line, which is the extremity of a surface.
4
Summarize the proof
In your own words, summarize how the existence of the point is established and why it is indivisible.

النوع الثاني : ( من حجة جمهور المتكلمين على ما ذهبوا إليه ( أن نبين تركب الجسم منها ( أي من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ( ابتداء ) أي من غير استعانة بأن كل قابل للانقسام فهو منقسم بالفعل كما في النوع الأول، وأما كون تلك الأجزاء متناهية فهو ظاهر أو معلوم مما مر آنفا ( وهو وجوه ( سبعة : ( الأول : النقطة ) وهـ تنقسم ( موجودة إذ بها تماس الخطوط والخطوط بها تماس السطوح والسطوح بها تماس الأجسام وتماس الموجودين بالمعدوم ضروري البطلان ) يعني لا شبهة في أن الأجسام موجودة وأنها تماس بأمور موجودة منقسمة في الطول والعرض دون العمق وإلا لزم التداخل بين المنقسمين في العمق أو كون التماس بجزأين منهما لا بهما فينقل الكلام إلى ذينك الجزأين وعدم انقسامهما ولا يتسلسل بل ينتهي إلى ما لا ينقسم في العمق وذلك هو السطح فثبت وجوده. ثم إن السطحين الموجودين يتماسان على أمر منقسم في الطول دون العرض، وإلا لزم أحد الأمرين كما عرفت وذلك هو الخط فثبت وجوده أيضاً. ثم إن الخطين الموجودين يتماسان على أمر ذي وضع لا ينقسم أصلا وهو النقطة، ( وأيضاً فإنها ) أي النقطة طرف للخط وهو للسطح وهو للجسم وطرف الموجود موجود ) فتكون النقطة موجودة ( ثم إنها لا تنقسم أصلاً . ( قلنا : في الجسم موجود ذو وضع لا ينقسم فإن كان جوهراً فهو المطلوب ) لأن ذلك الجوهر الذي لا يقبل الانقسام بوجه من الوجوه جزء للجسم، ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم يكن جوهراً بل عرضاً ( لكان له محل لا ينقسم وإلا انقسم الحال فيه لما مر مراراً ) وذلك المحل إن كان جوهراً فذاك وإن كان عرضاً كان له محل آخر ( ولا يتسلسل بل ينتهي إلى جوهر كذلك أي غير منقسم ( وهو الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ ). وقد وقع جزءا للجسم ثم إذا أخرجناه عن الجسم واعتبرنا التماس بالقياس إلى ما كان مجاوراً له وهكذا ظهر أن أجزاءه كلها جواهر غير قابلة للانقسام كما هو مطلوبنا وقد أجابوا عن ذلك بأن النقطة عرض غير سار في محله فلا يلزم من انقسام محلها انقسامها بل الأطراف كلها أعراض لكن الخط سار في محله في جهة واحدة فينقسم في هذه الجهة فقط والسطح سار في جهتين فينقسم فيهما فقط والنقطة لا سريان لها فلا انقسام فيها.
The second type (of the proof of the majority of the mutakallimun for what they held) is that we show that the body is composed of them (i.e., of the parts that are not further divisible) from the beginning (i.e., without recourse to [the premise that] everything divisible is actually divided, as in the first type). And that those parts are finite is apparent or known from what has just passed. And it has seven aspects: The first: The point — and it is divided? — exists, because by it lines touch, and by lines surfaces touch, and by surfaces bodies touch, and the touching of two existents by a non-existent is necessarily false. That is, there is no doubt that bodies exist and that they touch by means of existent things that are divisible in length and width but not in depth; otherwise there would be either interpenetration between the two divisible things in depth, or the touching would be by two parts of them [the touching things] not by the things themselves, and the discussion would be transferred to those two parts and their indivisibility. And there is no infinite regress, but it ends in that which is not divisible in depth, and that is the surface; so its existence is established. Then the two existing surfaces touch upon a thing divisible in length but not in width; otherwise one of the two [undesirable] things would follow as you know, and that is the line; so its existence also is established. Then the two existing lines touch upon a thing having a position that is not divisible at all, and that is the point. (And also, because) the point is an extremity of the line, which is an extremity of the surface, which is an extremity of the body, and the extremity of an existent is existent. Thus the point exists. Then it is not divisible at all. (We say:) In the body there exists something having position that is not divisible. If it is a substance, then that is what is sought (because that substance which does not accept division in any respect is a part of the body). Otherwise (i.e., if it is not a substance but an accident), then it has a substrate that is not divisible; otherwise the accident would be divided as the substrate is divided, as has been repeated many times. That substrate, if it is a substance, then it is the sought; and if it is an accident, it has another substrate, and there is no infinite regress, but it ends at a substance that is likewise not divided, and that is the indivisible part. And it has become a part of the body; then if we remove it from the body and consider the touching in relation to what was adjacent to it, and so on, it becomes apparent that all its parts are indivisible substances, as is our claim. And they have answered that the point is an accident that does not permeate its substrate, so the division of its substrate does not necessitate its division; rather, all extremities are accidents. But the line permeates its substrate in one dimension, so it divides only in that dimension; the surface permeates in two dimensions, so it divides only in them; and the point has no permeation, so there is no division in it.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of proof used by the majority of mutakallimun to establish that bodies are composed of indivisible parts (atoms). The passage begins by stating that unlike the first type, this proof does not rely on the premise that everything divisible is actually divided; rather, it directly demonstrates that bodies are composed of such parts from the outset (initially). The finitude of those parts is taken as apparent or already known. The proof is then unfolded through seven aspects (وجوه), of which the first is detailed here: the existence of the point. The argument proceeds as follows: bodies exist and touch each other. Touching must occur by something existent. Since bodies have dimensions (length, width, depth), their surfaces (which lack depth) exist, then lines (which have length but not width) exist, and finally points (which have no dimension at all) exist as the extremities of lines. The point is indivisible because it has no extension. But does this prove an atom? The passage then constructs a further argument: since the point is a non-permeating accident (according to the reply of the philosophers), it must inhere in a substance that is indivisible. If the point were an accident, its substrate would also be indivisible; this chain ends in a substance that is not divisible, i.e., the indivisible atom that is a part of the body. The passage also records the philosophers' objection that the point is an accident that does not permeate its substrate, so division of its substrate does not entail division of the point. The mutakallimun respond by distinguishing between accidents that permeate (like whiteness in a body) and those that do not (like points). Since the point does not permeate, its indivisibility does not require an indivisible substrate. However, the mutakallimun's main point is that the existence of the point as an extremity necessitates an indivisible locus, which is the sought-after atom. The passage ends by noting that this reasoning shows all parts of a body are indivisible substances.

Key Terms
النقطة
التماس
السطح
الخط
الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The point itself is the atom (the indivisible part of the body).
Correction: The point is an accident (non-permeating), not a substance. The atom is a substance that underlies the point.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first step in the touch chain that establishes the existence of the surface?
A) Lines touch surfaces.
B) Bodies touch surfaces.
C) Points touch lines.
D) Surfaces touch lines.

Key Takeaway
The existence of the point is established through the necessary chain of touch, and it is indivisible because it lacks extension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the point exists because it is the extremity of the line. Your life has an extremity too — death. Are you living as if that endpoint is as real as the point in this proof? What would change if you truly internalised that every moment brings you closer to that indivisible limit?
?
The argument shows that touch requires an existent mediator. In your relationship with Allah, what mediates your 'touch' — your connection to Him? Is it sincere devotion, or are you relying on something non-existent like mere habit? What step can you take today to ensure your connection is real and existent?

intermediate
6 min
The Point Requires an Indivisible Substance
Al-Jurjani argues that the point, being an indivisible extremity, must inhere in an indivisible substance, thus proving the atom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the point, as an indivisible accident, necessitates an indivisible substance (the atom) as its substrate, and how the philosophers' objection is addressed.

Core Idea
An indivisible point must inhere in an indivisible substance.

After establishing the existence of the point, al-Jurjani turns to its metaphysical implications. Since the point is an indivisible accident, it requires a substrate that is likewise indivisible. This substrate must be a substance, leading to the conclusion that the body contains an indivisible atom. The passage also addresses the objection that the point is a non-permeating accident, so its indivisibility does not force the substrate's indivisibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the logical structure: what is claimed, the reasoning, and the objection.
The passage starts with 'قلنا' (We say), indicating a direct argument.
2
Follow the argument for an indivisible substance
Identify the claim: in the body there exists something with position that is not divisible. Then the reasoning: if it is a substance, that is the sought atom; if it is an accident, it has a substrate that must be indivisible to avoid regress.
The argument uses the principle that an accident cannot be divided if its substrate is divided unless the accident permeates.
3
Understand the philosophers' objection
The objection states that the point is an accident that does not permeate its substrate, so division of the substrate does not imply division of the point. The mutakallimun respond by distinguishing permeating vs. non-permeating accidents.
The response reaffirms that the point's indivisibility is due to lack of permeation, but the substance must still be indivisible because the point inheres in it.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that all parts of the body are indivisible substances, as required by the mutakallimun's thesis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The point's indivisibility directly proves the atom without any further argument.
Correction: The point is an accident; its indivisibility only necessitates an indivisible substrate, which leads to the atom (substance).

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers' objection mentioned in the passage, why does the division of the substrate not necessitate the division of the point?
A) Because the point is a substance.
B) Because the point does not permeate its substrate.
C) Because the point is an essential property.
D) Because the point is a line.

Key Takeaway
The indivisibility of the point points to an indivisible substance (the atom) that serves as its substrate, and this conclusion is not undermined by the point being a non-permeating accident.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just followed a rational argument that begins with a point—something you cannot see—and ends with the existence of an unseen substance that forms the foundation of all material things. Are you willing to let such a philosophical proof reshape your understanding of reality, or do you dismiss it as abstract? What unseen truths have you accepted today based solely on reason?
?
The philosophers in this lesson deny that a point requires an indivisible substrate. Their objection seems plausible: if the point does not permeate, why can't the substrate be divided? When you face an argument that contradicts your assumptions, do you engage it seriously or retreat into comfortable skepticism? What would it cost you to follow the mutakallimun's reasoning to its conclusion about the nature of the world?
?
This lesson argues that the existence of a point forces you to accept an atom—a fundamental particle that cannot be split. If such a simple entity demands your intellectual submission, what about the more complex realities of Allah's attributes and the Hereafter? Is it possible that you have accepted the atom in theory but resisted other unseen truths that are equally well-argued? Examine your heart: where are you refusing to follow the evidence?

The Second Aspect: Motion as Evidence for the Atom
Al-Jurjani argues that motion's present part must exist, implying indivisible atoms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the existence of motion, divided into past, present, and future, leads to the necessity of an indivisible present part, supporting the atomist doctrine.

Core Idea
Motion's present part must exist and be indivisible, proving the atom.

In this passage, al-Jurjani presents the second argument for the existence of atoms, based on motion. He starts from the undeniable fact that motion exists, then divides it into three temporal parts. By examining the present part of motion, he shows that it must exist and be indivisible, implying that time and body are composed of indivisible atoms. This argument is a cornerstone of the kalam cosmological proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the argument is presented in a compact logical style.
2
Identify the three parts of motion
Motion is divided into present, past, and future. Understand the definitions: past is what was present, future is what will be present.
This division is crucial for the argument.
3
Understand why the present part must exist
The passage argues that if the present part did not exist, motion would be non-existent entirely, because past and future are non-existent. Since motion does exist, the present part must exist.
This is the core inference.
4
Grasp the implication for atomism
The present part of motion is an indivisible 'now', analogous to indivisible atoms of time and space. This supports the doctrine that bodies are composed of indivisible atoms.
This connects to the broader kalam proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه ( الثاني : الحركة موجودة) بالضرورة، ( وإنها تنقسم إلى حاضرة وماضية ومستقبلة . فنقول : إن الحاضرة منها موجودة وإلا لم يوجد الماضي ) منها ( ولا المستقبل لأن الماضي ما كان حاضراً والمستقبل ما سيحضر ) . ولا شك أن الماضي منها لا وجود له حال كونه ماضياً ولا المستقبل حال كونه مستقبلاً، فإذا لم تكن الحاضرة موجودة لم تكن الحركة موجودة أصلاً لأن الماضي والمستقبل معدومان لأن الماضي صار معدوماً والمستقبل لم يوجد أصلاً، وهذا التقرير لا يحتاج إلى أخذ ما ذكره المصنف رحمه الله.
The second aspect: Motion exists necessarily, and it is divided into present, past, and future. So we say: The present part of it exists; otherwise the past would not exist, nor the future, because the past is what was present and the future is what will be present. And there is no doubt that the past has no existence while being past, nor the future while being future. Therefore if the present did not exist, motion would not exist at all, because the past and future are non-existent, since the past has become non-existent and the future has not yet existed. And this explanation does not need to take what the author (may God have mercy on him) mentioned.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage presents the second of the seven aspects (وجوه) in the mutakallimun's proof for atoms, based on motion. The argument begins with the premise that motion exists necessarily (by immediate awareness). Motion is then divided into three temporal parts: present, past, and future. The key claim is that the present part of motion must exist; otherwise, the past and future would not exist, because the past is defined as what was once present, and the future is defined as what will be present. Since past motion is non-existent now, and future motion is also non-existent now, the only existent part of motion is the present. If the present part did not exist, motion would be entirely non-existent, which is impossible given that motion does exist. The implication for atomism is that this present part of motion must be indivisible (like a 'now' in time), paralleling the indivisible parts of space/body. The passage ends noting that this explanation does not require additional details from the author (al-Iji). The argument is incomplete in the window, but the core idea is that motion's existence entails a present that is not further divisible, supporting the atomic theory of time and consequently of bodies.

Key Terms
الحركة (al-haraka)
الحاضرة (al-hādira)
الماضي (al-māḍī)
المستقبل (al-mustaqbal)
الآن (al-ān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument only proves time atoms, not spatial atoms.
Correction: The argument is part of a broader proof that time and space are composed of indivisible parts (jawhar), and the indivisible present of motion directly supports the existence of indivisible substances.

Checkpoint
What does the passage claim would happen if the present part of motion did not exist?
A) Motion would still exist through the past and future.
B) Motion would be non-existent entirely.
C) The past would become present.
D) The future would be impossible.

Key Takeaway
The existence of motion necessitates an indivisible present part, which is a key premise in the kalam argument for atoms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the present moment is the only part of motion that truly exists, are you living in this moment or distracted by past regrets and future worries? What one concrete action can you take today to be fully present in your awareness of Allah during your salah?
?
This argument shows that motion is built on indivisible 'nows'. In your spiritual life, do you treat each act of worship as a discrete, fully present moment before Allah, or do you rush through them mindlessly? What is one way you can improve the quality of your present attention in worship from today?
?
The present part of motion must exist for motion to be real. Is your faith a living, present reality in your life right now, or is it merely a memory of the past or a hope for the future? What step will you take this week to make your iman more 'present' and active?

The Mutakallimun's Proof of Indivisible Contact
Proof that sphere-plane contact is indivisible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutakallimun's proof that the contact point of a sphere with a plane must be indivisible, and how this leads to the conclusion that matter is composed of indivisible parts (atoms).

Core Idea
A true sphere cannot touch a plane with a line or surface — only an indivisible point.

This passage presents a key argument from the mutakallimun (Islamic theologians) to prove the existence of indivisible atoms. By analyzing how a sphere contacts a plane, the argument rules out division of the touching part and concludes it must be indivisible. This line of reasoning underpins the atomistic conception of matter in classical Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Carefully read the Arabic text, then the English translation. Notice the logical structure: it starts with a conditional, then a contradiction, then the conclusion.
The heading is partially missing but the content is clear.
2
Understand the first part: the contradiction
The argument assumes the touching part is divisible. If it divides in one direction it becomes a line; if in two, a surface. But a line or surface on the sphere would make it flat, contradicting its spherical nature.
This proves the touching part must be indivisible.
3
Follow the rolling argument
Now imagine the sphere rolls along the plane, touching it with all its parts. Since each contact point is indivisible, every part of the sphere's surface and the plane is indivisible, implying atomism.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The proof establishes that matter consists of indivisible parts. This is a foundational argument for the mutakallimun's atomism.
Think about why this matters for theology: it defends divine omnipotence over material necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الأول - المقصد الرابع: حجة المتكلمين على [؟] به المماسة ) بينهما ) لا ينقسم وإلا فإما ) أن ينقسم ( في جهة ) واحدة ( فهو خط أو ) في أكثر) يعني في جهتين ( فهو سطح ولانطباقه ) أي ولانطباق ما به المماسة من الكرة ( على السطح المستوى فهو مستو سواء كان خطأ أو سطحاً ( فلا تكون الكرة ) المفروضة ( كرة ) حقيقية لاستحالة أن يوجد على محيطها خط مستقيم أو سطح مستو بالضرورة ( هذا خلف) . فتعين أن يكون ما به المماسة فيهما أمراً غير منقسم ( ثم نفرض تدحرجها على السطح) المستوي ( بحيث تماسه بجميع أجزائها فتكون جميع الأجزاء من ظاهر الكرة ومن ذلك السطح ( غير منقسمة) وكذا الحال الأجزاء التي في أعماقها ) وهو المطلوب ) .
First Observatory - Fourth Section: The proof of the mutakallimun regarding [?]. The touching part (between them) is not divisible; otherwise, if it divides in one direction, it is a line, or in more (i.e., two directions), it is a surface. And because of the coincidence of the touching part of the sphere with the plane, it is flat, whether it is a line or a surface. So the supposed sphere is not a true sphere, because it is impossible by necessity for a straight line or a flat surface to exist on its circumference. This is a contradiction. Therefore it is determined that the touching part in them is an indivisible thing. Then we suppose its rolling on the plane such that it touches it with all its parts, so all the parts of the sphere's surface and that plane are indivisible. Likewise the parts in its depths. That is what was desired.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents the mutakallimun's proof that the point of contact between a sphere and a plane must be indivisible. The argument proceeds by contradiction: if the touching part were divisible, then the division would be either in one direction (making a line) or two (making a surface). But a line or surface on the sphere's circumference would make it flat, which is impossible for a true sphere. Hence the touching part is indivisible. Then, by supposing the sphere rolls along the plane, touching it at all parts, it follows that all parts of both surfaces are indivisible, leading to the conclusion that matter is composed of indivisible parts (atoms).

Key Terms
المماسة
غير منقسم
خط
سطح
كرة
محیط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof assumes the sphere actually becomes flat when touching.
Correction: The proof only says that if the touching part were divisible, then by coincidence the sphere would have to be flat, which contradicts its nature. The sphere remains a true sphere; the contradiction shows the touching part cannot be divisible.

Checkpoint
What would the touching part become if it divided in one direction?
A) A point
B) A line
C) A surface
D) A body

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun prove the existence of indivisible atoms by showing that the contact between a sphere and a plane must be at an indivisible point, and this indivisibility extends to all parts of matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The mutakallimun used logic to prove that matter is made of indivisible atoms. If every part of your physical existence is built from such atoms, each bearing the mark of its Creator's design, how does that change the way you view your own body and the world around you? What would it take for you to see every 'atom' of your daily life as a sign pointing to Him?
?
The proof shows that a 'true sphere' cannot have any flat part; it must be perfectly consistent. Consider your own faith: are there areas where your belief is 'flat' — inconsistent with the truth you claim to hold? What would it mean for your faith to be like that sphere, with every point indivisible and perfectly aligned with the truth of Allah's oneness?
?
This lesson uses a physical example to reach a conclusion about the unseen (atoms). If you are convinced by this logical proof, what other unseen realities (like the angels, the Day of Judgment) should you also accept on the basis of sound reasoning from revelation? How can you train your mind to embrace proofs that lead you to greater certainty in the unseen?

The Seventh Argument for Atomism and Its Refutation
Al-Jurjani presents the seventh argument for the indivisible part and refutes it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh argument for atomism, its two versions, and the key refutation based on the distinction between potential and actual infinite division.

Core Idea
Infinite division remains potential; actual infinite is impossible.

This lesson examines the seventh argument for the existence of the indivisible part (atom), presented by al-Jurjani. The argument attempts to prove atomism by showing that infinite division leads to absurd consequences. You will see two versions of the reductio and their refutation, which hinges on the difference between potential and actual existence of parts. The author then offers a concluding reflection on the persuasive value of such arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the full argument and refutation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow: the two arguments and their refutations. Then read the translation carefully.
Notice the structure: first argument, objection, second argument, refutation, final remark.
2
Analyze the first reductio (heaven vs. mustard seed)
The first argument says if no atoms, then parts of heaven and mustard seed are infinite in number and thus equal—an obvious falsehood. The objection points out that equality in number doesn't mean equality in magnitude.
3
Analyze the second reductio (infinite plates)
The second argument strengthens the first: infinite plates from a mustard seed would cover the earth and sky, which is impossible. The refutation states that infinite division is only potential; all those plates never become actual.
Note the phrase 'impossibility of all the divisions coming into actual existence, or even being assumed.'
4
Reflect on the author's concluding remark
Al-Jurjani says that although these arguments can be answered dialectically, they provide conviction for the fair-minded. Consider what he means by 'inner reassurance'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لولا انتهاء الأجسام إلى أجزاء لا تتجزأ لكان الانقسام في السماء والخردلة ذاهباً إلى غير النهاية فتكون أجزاؤهما الممكنة سواء لأن أجزاء كل واحدة منهما غير متناهية حينئذ وهو بديهي البطلان ويرد عليه أن الأجزاء فيهما وإن كانت غير متناهية بالمعنى الذي عرفت إلا أن مقادير أجزاء السماء ليست كمقادير أجزاء الخردلة فلا استحالة. الوجه السابع: لولا الجزء وانتهاء تقسيم الجسم إليه لكان يمكن أن تقسم الخردلة إلى صفائح غير متناهية فتغمر تلك الصفائح وجه الأرض وتستر وجوه السموات وتفضل عليها بما لا يتناهى وأنه ضروري البطلان. ورد هذا بما عرفت من معنى لا تناهي الانقسام وامتناع خروج جميع الأقسام إلى الفعل وجوداً بل فرضاً أيضاً، قال المصنف: وبعض ذلك الذي ذكرناه من حجج المتكلمين على إثبات الجزء وتركب الجسم منه وإن كان يمكن الجواب عنه جدلاً ففيه للمنصف إقناع وطمأنينة باطن فارجع أنت إلى إنصافك في الأجوبة التي مر ذكرها.
If bodies did not terminate in indivisible parts, then division in the heaven and the mustard seed would go on infinitely, and thus their possible parts would be equal, because the parts of each of them would then be infinite—which is obviously false. It is objected that although the parts in them are infinite in the sense you know, yet the magnitudes of the parts of heaven are not like the magnitudes of the parts of the mustard seed, so no absurdity arises. The seventh argument: If there were no indivisible part terminating the division of body, it would be possible to divide the mustard seed into infinite plates, and those plates would cover the face of the earth, screen the faces of the heavens, and exceed them infinitely—which is necessarily false. This is refuted by what you know of the meaning of infinite division and the impossibility of all the divisions coming into actual existence, or even being assumed. The author said: 'And some of what we have mentioned from the arguments of the theologians for proving the part and that the body is composed of it—although it can be answered dialectically—yet for the fair-minded person it contains conviction and inner reassurance. So refer to your own sense of fairness regarding the answers that have been mentioned.'
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh argument for the existence of the indivisible part (al-juz' alladhi la yatajazza'), followed by its refutation and a concluding remark by the author. The argument is a reductio: if bodies were infinitely divisible, then the parts of a heaven and a mustard seed would both be infinite in number, and thus equal—which is absurd. But the objector replies that equality in number does not entail equality in magnitude; the parts of heaven are larger. Then a stronger version is given: from an infinite division of a mustard seed, infinite plates would cover the entire universe, which is impossible. The refutation invokes the distinction between potential and actual infinite division: even assuming infinite division, the actual existence of all those plates is impossible, so the consequence does not follow. The author then notes that although these arguments can be countered dialectically, they still provide conviction and inner satisfaction for the fair-minded person, inviting the reader to judge the answers fairly.

Key Terms
جزء لا يتجزأ
انقسام إلى غير النهاية
قوة وفعل
بديهي البطلان
إقناع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The refutation admits that infinite division is actually possible, but denies the absurd consequence.
Correction: The refutation explicitly states that infinite division is not actually possible; it is only potential. Therefore the absurd consequence (e.g., infinite plates covering the earth) does not arise.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the refutation of the seventh argument?
A) The parts of heaven and mustard seed are equal in number.
B) The infinite plates would actually exist and cover the earth.
C) The infinite division is only potential, not actual, so the consequence does not follow.
D) The mustard seed cannot be divided infinitely because it is too small.

Key Takeaway
The seventh argument for atomism fails because infinite division is only potential, not actual, so the absurd consequences never materialize.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Did you honestly weigh it, or did you look for ways to dismiss it? What would it look like for you to be truly fair-minded in matters of faith from now on?
?
This refutation hinges on the difference between potential and actual infinite. In your spiritual life, are there areas where you have kept good intentions or resolutions as mere possibilities—never actualized—while convincing yourself they are real? What is one thing you have been postponing that needs to move from potential to actual today?
?
Al-Jurjani says these proofs carry inner reassurance for the fair-minded. Have you ever felt your heart settle into certainty through a rational argument—or does your faith rest on something else? If you seek that inner conviction, what would it cost you to honestly engage with such proofs instead of avoiding them?
