The First Argument for Hyle: Shape as an Attribute of Existence
Presents the first argument for hyle: shape is a necessary attribute of existence, not quiddity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why hypothetical parts of a body do not require shape, based on the distinction between attributes of existence and quiddity.

Core Idea
Shape is a consequence of existence, not of quiddity.

In defending the existence of hyle (matter) within a body, scholars like al-Iji face a counterexample: If a simple body like a celestial sphere has no parts, how can it be composed of matter and form? This passage presents the first argument that shape, and thus composition, is a necessary attribute of existence, not of the essence (quiddity). By understanding this distinction, we can see why hypothetical mental parts don't require shape.

Guided Path
1
Understand the counterexample
The counterexample supposes a whole and its hypothetical parts; the objection is that if a simple body has no parts, it cannot have shape or composition.
2
Recognize the key distinction
The author argues that shape is a necessary attribute of existence (al-wujud), not of quiddity (al-mahiyya). This means shape only applies to things that exist externally, not to mental concepts.
3
See how the distinction refutes the objection
Since hypothetical parts exist only in the mind, they lack external existence, so they do not require shape. Additionally, partiality itself prevents equality in shape and magnitude, and bodily form stripped of matter yields no differentiation.
The conclusion is that the counterexample is repelled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الأول - المقصد الثامن : إثبات الهيولى في الجسم
المفروض بعد وجود الكل ورد بأن الشكل من لوازم الوجود دون الماهية، فإذا اقتضاه طبيعة لم يكن اقتضاؤها إياه إلا في الخارج، فلا يلزم ثبوته للأجزاء المفروضة فلا يتجه السؤال وأيضاً الجزئية مطلقاً مانعة من المساواة في الشكل والمقدار معاً، فلا مدخل لتأخر الجزء في الوجود عن الكل في المانعية ( وأما الصورة ) الجمسية ( فلو تجردت ) عن المادة (فلا تكون هناك إلا الطبيعة الجسمية ( المشتركة)، ولم يكن هناك سبب يقتضي كلية وجزئية سوى تلك الطبيعة المشتركة، فلا يتصور حينئذ اختلاف في أمر من الأمور حتى في الكلية والجزئية ( فلا يكون ثمة كل ولا فضلاً اختلافهما بالشكل فقد اندفع عن الدليل النقض المذكور
The First Observation – Eighth Aim: Proving Hyle in the Body.
The supposition after the existence of the whole is rejected by [saying] that shape is among the necessary attributes of existence, not quiddity. So if a nature necessitates it, its necessitation of it is only in external [existence]; thus its being established for the hypothetical parts is not necessary, so the question does not arise. Also, partiality absolutely prevents equality in both shape and magnitude, so the delay of the part in existence from the whole has no bearing on the prevention. (As for the) bodily (form), if it is stripped (of matter), then there is nothing there except the (common) bodily nature, and there is no cause that necessitates wholeness and partiality other than that common nature. Thus no difference is conceivable in any matter, even in wholeness and partiality, (so there is no whole, let alone their difference in shape). So the mentioned counterexample is repelled from the proof.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents the first argument for the existence of hyle (matter) in a body, responding to a counterexample involving hypothetical parts of a simple body like the celestial sphere. The author states that shape (al-shakl) is a necessary attribute of existence (al-wujud) not quiddity (al-mahiyya). Therefore, if a nature (such as bodyness) necessitates a particular shape, it does so only in external existence, not in the mind. Hence hypothetical parts that have no external existence are not required to have that shape. Additionally, partiality (al-juz'iyya) itself prevents equality in shape and magnitude, so the fact that a part comes after the whole in existence does not affect this. The passage then considers the bodily form (al-sura al-jismiyya) if stripped of matter: only the common bodily nature remains, with no cause for distinction between whole and part, so no whole or part exists, and consequently no difference in shape. Thus the counterexample is refuted.

اللوازم
الوجود
الماهية
الجزئية

الصورة الجسمية
الهيولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Confusing necessary attributes of existence with attributes of quiddity; shape is inherent in the essence (quiddity) of a body.
Correction: Shape is a necessary attribute of existence (al-wujud), not of quiddity (al-mahiyya). It only manifests in external existence, not in mental conception.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that hypothetical parts do not require shape?
A) Because shape is a necessary attribute of quiddity, not existence.
B) Because shape is a necessary attribute of existence, not quiddity, and hypothetical parts only exist in the mind.
C) Because shape is accidental and can be separated.
D) Because partiality prevents equality in shape.

Key Takeaway
The first argument for hyle establishes that shape is a necessary attribute of existence, not quiddity, so hypothetical mental parts do not require shape, and the counterexample fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that the outward shape or appearance of a thing (including yourself) is part of its true essence? How might this mistake lead you to overvalue appearances or judge others unfairly?
?
This lesson argues that shape is not found in quiddity but only in external existence. In your own life, what are some attributes you treat as essential to your identity that are actually just consequences of your existence? How does this distinction affect your understanding of change and permanence?
?
If you mentally stripped away all matter from your conception of yourself, what would remain? Is your core self defined by your essence or by your existence? How does this affect your accountability before Allah, who knows both your essence and your existence?

The Second Way: Independence from Substrate
Sanusi presents the second argument for hyle's existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second way of proving hyle by showing that bodily form cannot be independent of a substrate.

Core Idea
Bodily form's inherence in matter proves it cannot exist without hyle.

After establishing the first way, the author presents a second argument: if the bodily form were stripped of hyle and existed by itself, it would be independent of any substrate. But since it is inherently in matter, it cannot be stripped. This argument relies on the inseparable relationship between form and matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the conditional structure: if form is stripped and subsists by itself, it would be independent and not inhere; but it actually inheres, so stripping is impossible.
2
Identify the logical structure
The argument is a conditional proof. Identify the premise (form inheres) and the conclusion (form cannot be stripped). The author mentions that the answer is known from earlier discussions.
The response to this argument is that the form is not essentially needy; but the argument still shows inherence is a necessary property.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: what does this argument assume about the nature of bodily form? It assumes that if form could exist without matter, it would not need a substrate. But our observation shows it always needs a substrate, so hyle is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : ( من الوجوه الثلاثة ( الصورة الجسمية (لو) خلت عن الهيولى و (قامت بذاتها لاستغنت في نفسها ( عن المحل فلا تحل فيه) أصلاً لكنها حالة فيه فلا يجوز حلولها عنه وقد عرفت جوابه . ( الثالث : ( من تلك الوجوه أن يقول : على تقدير أن يجوز خلو الصورة عن المادة ( نفرض الكل تفارقه صورته قبل التجزئة وبعدها فإن كان لا تميز ثمة بين صورة الكل وصورة الجزء ( فالشيء مع غيره كهو لا وإن كان ) بينهما تميز ( وقد عرفت ) في مباحث التعين ( أنه لا تميز) ولا تعدد
قوله : (تبدل إلخ) بل أصل الشكل إذا إحاطة الجد والحدود لا يتصور فيما لا امتداد ويقتضي القسمة الوهمية أي فيما له طبيعة نوعية متعددة الأفراد كما فيما نحن فيه . قوله : (كما مر من أن حكم الأمثال واحدة . قوله : ( وقد عرفت جوابه من أنه يجوز أن لا تكون محتاجة ولا مستعيرة . قوله: (فإن كان لا تميز (إلخ فيه أن الكلية والجزئية باعتبار المادة فإذا فرضت الصورة منفردة عن المادة فلا كل ولا جزء ولا تعدد فيها ولا يلزم أن يكون الشيء مع غيره كهو لا معه فتدبر . قوله : ( عن هذا الذي قلناه أي قوله : لأنا نقول إلخ . قوله : ( وقد عرفت جوابه وقد عرفت أيضاً ما في هذا الجواب من أنه لا واسطة بين الاحتياج الذاتي إلى المحل والغنى الذاتي عنه، وقد عرفت أيضاً ما ذكرنا في توجيه كلام المصنف . قوله : ( نفرض الكل تفارقه صورته المراد من الكل هاهنا المجموع المركب من الهيولى والصورة وقوله : صورته هذه الإضافة من قبيل إضافة الجزء إلى الكل ومعنى مفارقة الصورة عن الكل هو أن تبقى الصورة بدون الكل فتكون حينئذ مجردة عن الهيولى وقوله : قبل التجزئة وبعدها متعلق بقوله: تفارقه، ثم إن إمكان وقوع المجموع الذي فرضتم ممنوع في هوية الصورة التي فرض كونها مجردة عن الهيولى لا بد لإثباته من دليل .
Second: (Among the three ways) (The bodily form) if it is stripped of hyle and (subsists by itself), it would (be independent in itself) (of the substrate, so it would not inhere in it) at all, but it is inherent in it, so its inherence without it is not permissible. And you have known its answer.
Third: (Among those ways) that he says: On the assumption that the form can be stripped of matter, (we suppose the whole is separated from its form before and after division. If there is no distinction then between the form of the whole and the form of the part, (then the thing with another is like it without it; and if) there is distinction (and you have known) in the discussions of determination (that there is no distinction) and no multiplicity.
His statement: (Change etc.) Rather, the origin of shape, if it is the enclosure of boundaries, is not conceivable in what has no extension, and it requires imaginary division, i.e., in what has a specific nature with multiple individuals, as in our case.
His statement: (As passed, that the judgment of similar things is one.)
His statement: (And you have known its answer, that it is permissible that it is neither needy nor borrowing.)
His statement: (If there is no distinction etc.) In it [i.e., the argument] that wholeness and partiality are by virtue of matter; so if the form is supposed isolated from matter, then there is no whole, no part, and no multiplicity in it, and it does not follow that a thing with another is like it without it, so reflect.
His statement: (About this which we said, i.e., his statement: 'For we say' etc.)
His statement: (And you have known its answer, and you have also known what is in this answer that there is no intermediate between essential need for a substrate and essential independence from it, and you have also known what we mentioned in directing the author's statement.)
His statement: (We suppose the whole is separated from its form) The meaning of 'whole' here is the composite of hyle and form, and his statement 'its form' is an addition of the part to the whole. The meaning of the separation of the form from the whole is that the form remains without the whole, thus it is then stripped of hyle. His statement: 'before and after division' is related to his statement 'separates'. Then, the possibility of the occurrence of the composite which you supposed is denied in the identity of the form which is supposed to be stripped of hyle; it must be proven by evidence.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains the second and third ways of proving hyle. The second way states: if the bodily form were stripped of hyle and subsisted by itself, it would be independent of a substrate and would not inhere in anything; but in fact it does inhere in matter (hyle), so it cannot be stripped. The author notes that the answer to this is already known. The third way: assuming the form can be stripped of matter, we suppose the whole composite (matter+form) is separated from its form before and after division. If there is no distinction between the form of the whole and the form of the part, then a thing with another is like itself without it (which is absurd). If there is distinction, then we already know from discussions of determination that there is no distinction or multiplicity when the form is abstracted. The commentary clarifies key points: shape requires extension and imaginary division; wholeness and partiality depend on matter; the answer to the second way is that the form is neither essentially needy nor borrowing; and in the third way, the possibility of such a separation is itself denied unless proven.

الحلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Bodily form can exist independently without matter.
Correction: Bodily form is always inherent in matter; independence would require it to be non-necessary, but it is inherently material.

Checkpoint
What does the second way conclude about the bodily form?
A) It can exist without hyle.
B) It cannot be stripped of hyle because it inheres in matter.
C) It is independent and needs no substrate.
D) It is immaterial.

Key Takeaway
The second way proves hyle by showing bodily form's necessary inherence in a substrate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your own body is a bodily form that depends entirely on a substrate for its existence. In what area of your life have you been acting as if you are self-sufficient, independent of Allah's constant support? Write one concrete step to change that today.
?

The Third Way: Distinction of Parts
Sanusi presents the third argument for hyle through a distinction dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument for hyle based on distinctions between the form of the whole and the form of the part.

Core Idea
Without matter, whole and part forms would be indistinguishable, proving hyle's necessity.

The third way considers the scenario where form is separated from matter. The author supposes the whole composite (matter+form) is separated from its form before and after division. He then examines whether there is a distinction between the form of the whole and the form of the part. This leads to a dilemma that shows such separation is impossible without hyle.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothetical
The author asks us to suppose that the whole composite (matter+form) is stripped of its form, both before and after division. This means the form exists separately.
2
Analyze the two branches
There are two possibilities: either there is no distinction between the form of the whole and the form of the part, or there is distinction. If no distinction, then the thing with another is like it without it (absurd). If distinction, then earlier discussions on determination showed no distinction exists when form is abstracted.
3
Draw the conclusion
Both branches lead to problems, so the assumption that form can exist without matter is false. Hence, hyle must exist to account for distinctions between forms of wholes and parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

( الثالث : ( من تلك الوجوه أن يقول : على تقدير أن يجوز خلو الصورة عن المادة ( نفرض الكل تفارقه صورته قبل التجزئة وبعدها فإن كان لا تميز ثمة بين صورة الكل وصورة الجزء ( فالشيء مع غيره كهو لا وإن كان ) بينهما تميز ( وقد عرفت ) في مباحث التعين ( أنه لا تميز) ولا تعدد
قوله : (تبدل إلخ) بل أصل الشكل إذا إحاطة الجد والحدود لا يتصور فيما لا امتداد ويقتضي القسمة الوهمية أي فيما له طبيعة نوعية متعددة الأفراد كما فيما نحن فيه . قوله : (كما مر من أن حكم الأمثال واحدة . قوله : ( وقد عرفت جوابه من أنه يجوز أن لا تكون محتاجة ولا مستعيرة . قوله: (فإن كان لا تميز (إلخ فيه أن الكلية والجزئية باعتبار المادة فإذا فرضت الصورة منفردة عن المادة فلا كل ولا جزء ولا تعدد فيها ولا يلزم أن يكون الشيء مع غيره كهو لا معه فتدبر . قوله : ( عن هذا الذي قلناه أي قوله : لأنا نقول إلخ . قوله : ( وقد عرفت جوابه وقد عرفت أيضاً ما في هذا الجواب من أنه لا واسطة بين الاحتياج الذاتي إلى المحل والغنى الذاتي عنه، وقد عرفت أيضاً ما ذكرنا في توجيه كلام المصنف . قوله : ( نفرض الكل تفارقه صورته المراد من الكل هاهنا المجموع المركب من الهيولى والصورة وقوله : صورته هذه الإضافة من قبيل إضافة الجزء إلى الكل ومعنى مفارقة الصورة عن الكل هو أن تبقى الصورة بدون الكل فتكون حينئذ مجردة عن الهيولى وقوله : قبل التجزئة وبعدها متعلق بقوله: تفارقه، ثم إن إمكان وقوع المجموع الذي فرضتم ممنوع في هوية الصورة التي فرض كونها مجردة عن الهيولى لا بد لإثباته من دليل .
Second: (Among the three ways) (The bodily form) if it is stripped of hyle and (subsists by itself), it would (be independent in itself) (of the substrate, so it would not inhere in it) at all, but it is inherent in it, so its inherence without it is not permissible. And you have known its answer.
Third: (Among those ways) that he says: On the assumption that the form can be stripped of matter, (we suppose the whole is separated from its form before and after division. If there is no distinction then between the form of the whole and the form of the part, (then the thing with another is like it without it; and if) there is distinction (and you have known) in the discussions of determination (that there is no distinction) and no multiplicity.
His statement: (Change etc.) Rather, the origin of shape, if it is the enclosure of boundaries, is not conceivable in what has no extension, and it requires imaginary division, i.e., in what has a specific nature with multiple individuals, as in our case.
His statement: (As passed, that the judgment of similar things is one.)
His statement: (And you have known its answer, that it is permissible that it is neither needy nor borrowing.)
His statement: (If there is no distinction etc.) In it [i.e., the argument] that wholeness and partiality are by virtue of matter; so if the form is supposed isolated from matter, then there is no whole, no part, and no multiplicity in it, and it does not follow that a thing with another is like it without it, so reflect.
His statement: (About this which we said, i.e., his statement: 'For we say' etc.)
His statement: (And you have known its answer, and you have also known what is in this answer that there is no intermediate between essential need for a substrate and essential independence from it, and you have also known what we mentioned in directing the author's statement.)
His statement: (We suppose the whole is separated from its form) The meaning of 'whole' here is the composite of hyle and form, and his statement 'its form' is an addition of the part to the whole. The meaning of the separation of the form from the whole is that the form remains without the whole, thus it is then stripped of hyle. His statement: 'before and after division' is related to his statement 'separates'. Then, the possibility of the occurrence of the composite which you supposed is denied in the identity of the form which is supposed to be stripped of hyle; it must be proven by evidence.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains the second and third ways of proving hyle. The second way states: if the bodily form were stripped of hyle and subsisted by itself, it would be independent of a substrate and would not inhere in anything; but in fact it does inhere in matter (hyle), so it cannot be stripped. The author notes that the answer to this is already known. The third way: assuming the form can be stripped of matter, we suppose the whole composite (matter+form) is separated from its form before and after division. If there is no distinction between the form of the whole and the form of the part, then a thing with another is like itself without it (which is absurd). If there is distinction, then we already know from discussions of determination that there is no distinction or multiplicity when the form is abstracted. The commentary clarifies key points: shape requires extension and imaginary division; wholeness and partiality depend on matter; the answer to the second way is that the form is neither essentially needy nor borrowing; and in the third way, the possibility of such a separation is itself denied unless proven.

Two Arguments That Form Is Not a Cause of Matter
First two proofs that form is not a cause of matter, with a note on temporal simultaneity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two arguments from kalam demonstrating that form (al-ṣūra) cannot be a cause of matter (al-hayūlā), including the reasoning based on temporal priority and the observation of matter's persistence.

Core Idea
Form cannot cause matter because form is posterior and matter survives form's removal.

In this passage, the author presents two concise proofs to show that form is not the cause of matter. The first argument uses the relationship between form, finitude, and configuration, establishing that form is posterior to matter. The second argument appeals to empirical observation: when a specific form disappears, matter remains, disproving a causal relation. Understanding these arguments is crucial for grasping the independence of matter from form in the Aristotelian framework used by theologians.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal English translation. This will help you grasp the author's concise style.
Notice the author uses two separate 'also' (و) to introduce each argument.
2
Analyze the first argument (temporal priority)
Identify the steps: form only exists with finitude and configuration, which are accidents of matter and thus posterior; therefore, whatever is together with the posterior is itself posterior; so form is posterior to matter and cannot be its cause.
The author adds a nuance about temporal simultaneity versus other types of priority.
3
Analyze the second argument (persistence of matter)
Consider the hypothetical: if form were a cause of matter, then when that specific form disappears, matter should also disappear. But we observe that matter remains when forms change (e.g., through separation). Thus form is not a cause.
This is an empirical argument based on observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالأولى أن يقال : فلا تكون علة لوجود محلها (و) أيضاً ليست الصورة علة للهيولى ( لأنها ) أي الصورة ( لا توجد إلا مع التناهي والتشكل لما مر، ( والهيولي متقدمة عليهما ) لأنهما من توابع المادة المتأخرة عنها وما مع المتأخر متأخر كما أن ما مع المتقدم متقدم فتكون الصورة متأخرة عن الهيولى فلا تكون علة لها. ولا يخفى عليك أن الحكم بتأخر ما مع المتأخر إنما تظهر صحته في المعية والتأخر الزمانيين دون غيرهما، (و) أيضاً ليست الصورة علة للمادة ( للزوم انتفائها ) أي انتفاء المادة ( عند عدم الصورة المعينة) يعني لو كانت الصورة علة لها لانتفت عند انتفاء الصورة المعينة لوجوب انتفاء المعلول عند انتفاء علته لكن الصورة الجسمية تتبدل وتزول عند ورود الانفصال والهيولى باقية على حالها.
So it is better to say: it (form) is not a cause for the existence of its locus, and also the form is not a cause for matter because it (i.e., form) does not exist except with finitude and configuration, as has passed, and matter is prior to them because they are accidents of matter, posterior to it, and whatever is together with something posterior is posterior, just as whatever is together with something prior is prior. Thus form is posterior to matter, so it cannot be a cause for it. And it is not hidden from you that the judgment that what is together with the posterior is posterior only appears correct in temporal simultaneity and posteriority, not in other types. And also form is not a cause for matter because of the necessary non-existence of matter when a specific form is absent, meaning if form were its cause, matter would cease to exist when that specific form ceases, because the effect must cease when its cause ceases, but the corporeal form changes and disappears when separation occurs, while matter remains as it is.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents two arguments to prove that form (al-ṣūra) is not a cause (ʿilla) for matter (al-hayūlā). The first argument: form is posterior to matter because form only exists with finitude and configuration, which are accidental properties of matter and thus posterior to matter. Since whatever is together with what is posterior is itself posterior, form is posterior to matter and cannot be a cause (which must be prior). The author notes that this reasoning holds only for temporal simultaneity and posteriority, not for essential or ontological priority. The second argument: if a specific form were a cause of matter, then when that form is removed, matter should cease to exist. But we observe that when a corporeal form changes (e.g., through separation), matter remains. Therefore, form is not a cause. Both arguments are presented concisely.

علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that form is a cause of matter because matter depends on form for its identity.
Correction: The passage argues that form is not a cause because it is posterior to matter (temporally) and because matter persists even when a specific form changes. Causality requires priority and necessary connection, which is not observed between form and matter.

Checkpoint

A) Because form is prior to matter
B) Because form is posterior to matter
C) Because form is composite
D) Because form is accidental

Key Takeaway
Form cannot be a cause of matter because it is posterior to matter and matter remains when form changes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage argues that form is not a cause because matter survives even when form disappears. What forms or identities have you clung to that you thought were essential, but which have changed while you remained? How might letting go of those forms be a step toward recognizing what truly persists?
?
If form being posterior means it cannot cause matter, then reflect: are there goals or achievements you treat as the cause of your worth or happiness, when in fact they are effects of something deeper? What would it mean to reorder your priorities in light of true causality?

Objection and Answer: Specific vs Absolute Form
Objection and answer: specific form vs absolute form as cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the absolute form cannot be the cause of matter and how the principle that a one-in-person effect requires a one-in-person cause refutes the objection.

Core Idea
An individual thing needs an individual cause; a universal concept cannot cause a particular effect.

The argument that matter cannot exist without form seemed to establish that form is not a cause for matter. But an objector raises a subtle distinction: the argument only disproves the specific form, not form in general. In this passage, the author answers by invoking a key causal principle: a single individual requires a single individual cause. Let's see how that closes the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify what the objector claims: that the proof only applies to the specific form, not the absolute form.
The objector distinguishes between 'specific form' (al-ṣūra al-muʿayyana) and 'absolute form' (al-ṣūra al-muṭlaqa).
2
Examine the answer
Focus on the answer beginning with 'قلنا'. Notice the principle stated: the one in person must have its efficient cause one in person.
The answer does not reject the distinction but shows why absolute form cannot be a cause.
3
Apply the principle
Reflect: why is the absolute form not one in person? Because it is a universal concept, not an individual. Therefore, it cannot be the efficient cause of a particular matter.
This resolves the objection: the absolute form is ruled out by the nature of causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : ما ذكرتم إنما يدل على أن الصورة المعينة ليست علة لها ولا يلزم من عدم علية الصورة المعينة عدم علية الصورة المطلقة قلنا : الواحد بالشخص لا بد أن تكون علته الفاعلية واحدة بالشخص والصورة المطلقة ليست كذلك.
If it is said: what you have mentioned only indicates that the specific form is not a cause for it (matter), and it does not follow from the non-causality of the specific form the non-causality of the absolute form. We say: the one in person must have its efficient cause one in person, and the absolute form is not like that.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector argues that the previous proof only shows that a particular form (al-ṣūra al-muʿayyana) is not a cause for matter, but it does not rule out the absolute form (al-ṣūra al-muṭlaqa) as a cause. The answer replies that an individual thing (al-wāḥid bi-l-shakhṣ) must have a single efficient cause (ʿilla fāʿiliyya wāḥida bi-l-shakhṣ). The 'absolute form' is not one in person (it is a general concept), so it cannot be the cause of a particular matter. Thus, the objection fails.

Key Terms
صورة معينة
صورة مطلقة
علة فاعلية
واحد بالشخص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a universal concept (absolute form) could be an efficient cause of particular things.
Correction: An efficient cause must be an individual existent; universal concepts are not individual and cannot act as efficient causes.

Checkpoint
What is the answer to the objection that the argument only disproves specific form as cause?
A) Specific form is the only cause
B) Absolute form is not one in person, so cannot be a cause for a particular individual
C) Absolute form is more general, so it can be a cause
D) The objection is invalid because form is not a cause at all

Key Takeaway
A universal concept (absolute form) cannot be the efficient cause of a particular individual; only an individual cause can produce an individual effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you sometimes hide behind universal principles—like 'everyone sins' or 'God is merciful'—to avoid taking personal responsibility for your specific wrong actions? In light of this lesson, how can you make your repentance more individual and sincere today?
?
If a universal concept cannot cause an individual effect, then your faith cannot remain a mere abstract belief; it must manifest in concrete actions. What single concrete action will you perform today that proves your faith is not just a universal idea?
?
This principle reveals that your own choices are individual causes that produce individual results. Are you attributing your failures to vague excuses (like 'the system' or 'society') rather than owning them as your own? What individual cause are you ready to take responsibility for right now?

The Mutual Need Between Matter and Form
Proof of mutual dependency between matter and form.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why matter and form are mutually dependent: matter needs form for persistence, and form needs matter for individuation.

Core Idea
Matter and form are interdependent — neither can exist without the other.

In this passage, the author establishes a key metaphysical principle: matter (hayūlā) and form (ṣūra) are not independent principles but rely on each other for their existence and individuation. The argument uses the observation that they are always found together, which points to mutual need. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice the key terms: هيولى (matter), صورة (form), احتياج (need), بقاء (persistence), تشخص (individuation).
2
Understand the two-sided argument
The passage argues that matter needs form for persistence, and form needs matter for individuation. Identify these two claims.
3
Study the analogy of supports
The author uses an analogy of supports (daʿāʾim) being replaced to maintain a ceiling. Consider how this illustrates matter's need for successive forms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا تمهد هذا فنقول : التلازم وامتناع الانفكاك بينهما دل على الاحتياج من الجانبين ( فحاجة الهيولى إلى الصورة في بقائها لأن الصورة تستحفظها بتواردها عليها ( إذ لو فرضنا زوال صورة ) عنها ( وعدم اقتران ) صورة ( أخرى ) بها ( عدمت المادة ( لما مر من امتناع بقائها خالية عن الصور كلها ( فهي ) أي تلك الصور المتواردة عليها ) كالدعائم تزال واحدة منها عن ( واحدة ) منها عن السقف ) وتقام مقامها) دعامة (أخرى) فيكون السقف باقياً على حاله بتعاقب تلك الدعائم. ( وحاجة الصورة ) إلى الهيولى ( في التشخص والعوارض اللازمة لتشخصها ).
When this is established, we say: the mutual implication and impossibility of separation between them indicates need from both sides. So matter's need for form is for its persistence, because form preserves it by succeeding upon it. For if we suppose the removal of a form from it and no other form accompanies it, matter would cease to exist, because it cannot remain devoid of all forms. So those successive forms are like supports: one of them is removed from a wall? and another is put in its place, so the ceiling remains as it is through the succession of those supports. And form's need for matter is for individuation and the necessary accidents of its individuation.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage establishes the mutual need between matter (al-hayūlā) and form (al-ṣūra). Since they are always found together and cannot be separated, this indicates that each depends on the other. The need of matter for form is for its persistence: matter cannot exist without any form, so forms succeed one another to maintain matter, like supports (al-daʿāʾim) that are replaced one after another to keep a ceiling stable. The need of form for matter is for individuation (al-tashakhkhuṣ) and the accidents that necessarily accompany individuation. Thus, neither is the sole cause; they are interdependent.

Key Terms
هيولى
صورة
احتياج
بقاء
تشخص
تلازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think either matter or form is independent and self-sufficient.
Correction: The passage shows that they are interdependent in different respects: matter needs form for persistence, and form needs matter for individuation.

Checkpoint
Why does matter need form according to this passage?
A) For its original existence
B) For its persistence through successive forms
C) For its individuation
D) For its motion

Key Takeaway
Matter and form are mutually dependent: matter relies on form for its persistence, and form relies on matter for its individuation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your own body and soul are a composition that mirrors matter and form. In what specific ways do you currently act as if you are self-sufficient, forgetting that your persistence from moment to moment depends on a succession of gifts from your Creator? What would change if you consciously acknowledged your need for Him every hour?
?
The analogy of supports under a ceiling shows that you are constantly being preserved by successive 'supports' from Allah—your heartbeat, your breath, your sanity. Can you name three supports sustaining you right now that you have neglected to thank Him for? Will you thank Him for them aloud today?
?
If form cannot be individuated without matter, consider: your unique identity—your 'I'—is not self-standing. It is given to you by Allah through the particular composition He chose. How does this realization humble your pride? What is one way you can live today in the awareness that your very selfhood is a gift sustained by Him?

The Nine Universal Celestial Spheres
Lists the nine universal spheres in descending order with scriptural equivalents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nine universal celestial spheres in Islamic cosmology, their order, and their scriptural identifications.

Core Idea
The cosmos is a structured hierarchy of spheres, each with a name and place.

This passage from al-Mawaqif presents the enumeration of the nine universal celestial spheres as understood in Ptolemaic astronomy and integrated into Islamic theology. The author lists them from outermost to nearest, identifying some with scriptural terms like the Throne and Footstool.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage with translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the descending order from outermost to nearest.
2
Identify each sphere and its position
The passage enumerates nine spheres. List them in order and note any alternative names or descriptions given for each.
The first sphere has two additional names; the second is identified with the Footstool.
3
Note the scriptural identifications
The author explicitly links the outermost sphere to the 'Glorious Throne' and the sphere of fixed stars to the 'Footstool'. Reflect on how this merges natural philosophy with revelation.
This shows that the cosmos is not purely philosophical but grounded in scripture.
4
Understand the geocentric order
The spheres are arranged in a geocentric order, with the Earth at the center and the spheres moving outward. The last sphere mentioned, the 'lower heaven', is closest to us.
This order was standard in medieval Islamic astronomy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما التسعة الكلية فهي فلك الأفلاك (وهو المسمى) أيضاً عندهم (بالفلك الأطلس لأنه غير مكوكب ) على رأيهم (و) المسمى (بالعرش المجيد في لسان الشرع وتحته فلك الثوابت ) وهو الكرسي ( ثم فلك زحل ثم فلك المشتري، ثم فلك المريخ ثم فلك الشمس ، ثم فلك الزهرة ثم فلك عطارد ثم فلك السماء الدنيا ) لأنه أقرب إلينا من سائر الأفلاك.
As for the nine universal [spheres], they are: the sphere of spheres (which is also called by them the Atlas sphere because it is starless, in their view, and is called the Glorious Throne in the language of the Law), and beneath it the sphere of the fixed stars, which is the Footstool, then the sphere of Saturn, then the sphere of Jupiter, then the sphere of Mars, then the sphere of the Sun, then the sphere of Venus, then the sphere of Mercury, then the sphere of the lower heaven, because it is closer to us than the other spheres.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage enumerates the nine universal celestial spheres (al-aflāk al-kulliyya) that constitute the geocentric cosmos according to Ptolemaic astronomy, as adopted by Islamic theologians. The author lists them in descending order from the outermost to the nearest. The outermost is the 'sphere of spheres' (falk al-aflāk), also called the 'Atlas sphere' (al-falk al-aṭlas) because it contains no stars, and identified with the 'Glorious Throne' (al-arsh al-majīd) in scriptural language. Beneath it is the sphere of the fixed stars, equated with the 'Footstool' (al-kursiyy). Then follow the spheres of the seven planets in their traditional order: Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, Sun, Venus, Mercury, and finally the sphere of the lower heaven (al-samā' al-dunyā), which is the nearest of all. The passage thus provides a concise summary of the celestial hierarchy that forms the backdrop for theological discussions on divine creation and power.

Correction: The author explicitly identifies it with the 'Glorious Throne' (al-arsh al-majīd) in the language of the Law, showing that it has a scriptural basis.

Proof of Multiple Spheres from Diverse Movements
Proves the existence of multiple spheres from differences in motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that diverse celestial motions necessitate multiple spheres, each with its own essential movement.

Core Idea
Each distinct essential motion requires its own body.

The heavens display a variety of motions: different directions, speeds, or both. How can a single sphere produce such diversity? The theologians argue that it cannot—each essential motion must belong to its own subject. This short but powerful argument establishes the necessity of multiple celestial spheres, a key doctrine in classical cosmology.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the logical flow: observation of diverse movements → impossibility of one body having two essential motions → conclusion of multiple spheres.
Pay attention to the phrase 'حركتين ذاتيتين' (two essential movements).
2
Identify the two premises and the conclusion
Break the argument into: (1) we observe diverse movements, (2) a single body cannot have two essential movements, (3) therefore, multiple spheres exist.
This is a simple syllogism.
3
Reflect on the key terms
Understand 'حركة ذاتية' (essential movement) and 'متحرك على حدة' (its own mover). These are central to the argument.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question and try to explain the argument in your own words.
Check your answer against the feedback.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : ( دل على وجودها الحركات المختلفة في الجهة أو السرعة والبطء أو فيهما معاً ( فإنه لا بد لها ) أي لتلك الحركات من محال متعددة) إذ يستحيل أن يتحرك جسم واحد حركتين ذاتيتين، بل لا بد لكل حركة ذاتية من متحرك على حدة )
They said: 'Their existence is indicated by the diverse movements in direction, or speed and slowness, or in both together. For those movements must have multiple places (i.e., spheres), since it is impossible for a single body to have two essential movements; rather, each essential movement must have its own mover.'
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents a kalam argument for the existence of multiple celestial spheres (afāk). The argument starts from observational data: the heavens exhibit diverse movements—differences in direction (e.g., eastward vs. westward), in speed (fast vs. slow), or both. The author argues that such diversity cannot arise from a single body (jism wāḥid) because it is impossible for one body to have two essential (dhātiyya) movements simultaneously. Each essential movement requires its own distinct subject of motion (mutaḥarrik). Therefore, the observed variety of celestial motions necessitates the existence of multiple spheres, each with its own proper motion. This is a standard Aristotelian-Ptolemaic argument adopted by kalam theologians to explain the complexity of the heavens.

Key Terms
حركات مختلفة
حركة ذاتية
متحرك على حدة
محال متعددة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is about acceleration or deceleration within a single sphere.
Correction: The argument concerns essential movements (حركة ذاتية), not accidental changes in speed. Essential movements are inherent to the body's nature, not transient.

Checkpoint

B) Because the stars are fixed
C) Because the Quran mentions many heavens
D) Because the universe is eternal

Key Takeaway
The diversity of celestial motions rationally demands multiple spheres, since a single body cannot sustain two essential movements.

Proof of Order from Occultations and the Sun's Position
Proves the order of spheres through occultations and parallax.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how medieval astronomers used observations of occultations and parallax to infer the order of the celestial spheres, and why the Sun's position relative to Venus and Mercury required an approximation method.

Core Idea
Celestial order is revealed by which body hides which, and by parallax—but not all puzzles are solved by direct observation.

In this passage, the author presents a detailed argument for the arrangement of the planets based on which celestial bodies obscure one another. By examining occultations (ḥajab) and the phenomenon of parallax (ikhtilāf al-manẓar), astronomers were able to establish a clear hierarchy, except for the Sun's position relative to Venus and Mercury, which required a clever approximation. Let's explore this fascinating blend of observation and inference.

Guided Path
1
Read and consider the key observational findings
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting each observation: the Moon veils all planets, Mercury eclipses Venus, etc. This empirical data forms the backbone of the argument.
2
Understand the role of parallax
The Sun has parallax, unlike the superior planets. Parallax indicates the Sun is below those planets but above the Moon. Grasp how parallax serves as a distance indicator.
3
Identify the unresolved question
Why can't we determine whether the Sun is above or below Venus and Mercury from eclipses? The text explains that these planets are not visible at noon due to the Sun's rays. Consider the challenge.
4
Examine Ptolemy's approximation method
Ptolemy likened the Sun to a bead in a necklace, placed between the superior and inferior planets. Later, Ibn Sīnā claimed to have seen Venus and Mercury as spots on the Sun, supporting this view. Reflect on how this method works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فما هو أسفل يحجب ما هو أعلى أي يصير ساتراً له عنا إذا وقع على محاذاته ( وهو) أي الحجب ) على ما ذكرنا من الترتيب ) فإنهم وجدوا القمر يحجب سائر السيارة. ومن الثوابت ما هو على طريقته. فعلم أنه تحت الجميع ووجدوا عطارداً يكسف الزهرة، والزهرة المريخ والمريخ المشتري والمشتري زحل، وزحل بعض الثوابت، وأما الشمس فإنها لا تنكسف إلا بالقمر ولا يتصور كسفها بشيء من الكواكب لأنها تستتر بشعاعها إذا قربت منها، لكن لها اختلاف المنظر دون العلوية فهي تحتها وفوق القمر، وبقي الاشتباه في أنها فوق الزهرة وعطارد أو تحتها إذ لا سبيل إلى معرفة ذلك من الكسف لما عرفت من احتراقهما تحت الشعاع عند القرآن اختلاف المنظر لأنهما لا يبعدان عن الشمس كثيرا بعد، فلا يظهران عند كونهما على نصف النهار ليعلم بذات الشعبتين المنصوبة في سطح نصف النهار، أن لها اختلاف منظر أو لا، فلذلك عدل بطليموس إلى طريقة الاستحسان . فقال : هي كسمة القلادة متوسطة بين السبعة السيارة أعني بين العلوية وبين السفليتين والقمر. وقد تأكد هذا الرأي بما ذكره بعض المتأخرين كابن سينا ومن تقدمه من مقدمي هذه الصناعة أنه رأى الزهرة عند اجتماعها مع الشمس كشامة على صفحتها ومنهم من ادعى أنه رآها وعطارداً كشامتين عليها
And that which is lower veils what is higher, i.e., it becomes a screen for it from us when it aligns with it. And the veiling [occurs] according to the order we mentioned. For they found that the Moon veils all the other planets. And some of the fixed stars [veil in] the same way. So it is known that it (the Moon) is beneath all. And they found that Mercury eclipses Venus, Venus eclipses Mars, Mars eclipses Jupiter, Jupiter eclipses Saturn, and Saturn eclipses some of the fixed stars. As for the Sun, it is only eclipsed by the Moon, and its eclipse by any planet is inconceivable because it is concealed by its own rays when they approach it. However, the Sun has parallax (ikhtilāf al-manẓar) unlike the superior planets, so it is beneath them and above the Moon. There remains doubt whether it is above or below Venus and Mercury, because it cannot be known from eclipses, since those two planets burn up under the rays when in conjunction, and they do not appear when they are at noon to ascertain by the instrument with two prongs (dhāt al-shuʻbatayn) erected in the plane of the meridian whether they have parallax or not. Therefore, Ptolemy resorted to an approximation method, saying: 'It is like a necklace bead, situated in the middle of the seven planets, i.e., between the superior and the two inferior planets and the Moon.' This opinion was confirmed by what some later scholars, such as Ibn Sīnā and earlier masters of this craft, mentioned: that he saw Venus at its conjunction with the Sun as a mole on its disk, and some claimed that he saw it and Mercury as two moles on it.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage argues for the order of the spheres based on occultations (ḥajab), where a lower sphere hides a higher one. The author reports observational findings: the Moon veils all other planets, proving it is lowest. Mercury eclipses Venus, Venus Mars, Mars Jupiter, Jupiter Saturn, and Saturn some fixed stars, establishing their relative positions. The Sun presents a difficulty: it is only eclipsed by the Moon, not by any planet (since its brightness hides them), and it has parallax (ikhtilāf al-manẓar), indicating it is below the superior planets but above the Moon. However, its position relative to Venus and Mercury remains ambiguous because those planets are not visible at noon (due to proximity to the sun) to measure parallax with the instrument (dhāt al-shuʻbatayn). Ptolemy then used an approximation method, likening the Sun to a bead in a necklace, placed between the superior and inferior planets. Later astronomers like Ibn Sīnā claimed to have seen Venus and Mercury as spots on the Sun's disk during conjunction, supporting Ptolemy's view. This lesson demonstrates how empirical observations and instrumental measurements were used to infer the celestial order.

Key Terms
الحجب
الكسف
اختلاف المنظر
ذات الشعبتين
طريقة الاستحسان
كسمة القلادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage is primarily about solar eclipses.
Correction: The Arabic terms 'ḥajab' (veiling) and 'kisaf' (eclipse) are used broadly for any occultation, not just solar eclipses. The discussion focuses on one celestial body hiding another from view to infer their order.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Through occultations and parallax, medieval astronomers could determine the order of most planets, but the Sun's relation to Venus and Mercury required an approximation that was later confirmed by seeing spots on the Sun.

The astronomers looked at the heavens and saw order and design that pointed to a Creator. When was the last time you paused to truly observe the sky and felt that same awe? What is stopping you from seeing the signs that are right in front of you?

Ibn Sīnā and others claimed to witness planetary spots on the Sun—a testimony that later confirmed a theory. Whose trustworthy testimony about God's creation do you reject or ignore because it doesn't fit your preferred narrative? Are you humble enough to accept evidence that contradicts your assumptions?

The Impossibility of Piercing Spheres and the Ring Objection
Basis of proof and ring objection reply

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational basis for proving multiple celestial spheres: the impossibility of piercing spheres, and how the objection about planets moving on rings within one sphere is countered by analogy with eccentric spheres.

Core Idea
Spheres cannot be pierced; that is the logical anchor for multiple spheres.

The proof for the multiplicity of spheres begins with a simple but powerful premise: celestial spheres are impenetrable. If they could be pierced, a single sphere could contain all planets moving like swimmers. The author then anticipates an objection: why not have planets embedded in one sphere on movable rings? He defends the original proof by noting that such rings are no more exotic than the already accepted eccentric spheres.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on piercing impossibility
Read the first part where the author states the basis and the consequence if piercing were possible.
Notice the phrase 'لا تنخرق أصلاً' (cannot be pierced at all).
2
Understand the ring objection
The objector suggests planets could be on rings within one sphere, moving themselves or by the planets.
The rings are called 'نطاقات'.
3
Examine the author's reply
The author says this is not more far-fetched than eccentrics (الخارج المركز) and their complements.
This shows the argument is consistent with accepted astronomical models.
4
Reflect on the logical structure
Consider how the author uses a hypothetical (piercing) to establish a necessary truth, and then defends it against alternative models.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبناه ) أي مبنى ما ذكر من الدليل على تعدد الأفلاك هو ( أن الأفلاك لا تنخرق ( أصلاً ) وإلا جاز أن يكون هناك فلك واحد ساكن، ويكون ( الحركة للكوكب نفسه كالسابح في الماء، وإن سلم ذلك) أي امتناع الانخراق ( فلم لا يجوز أن تكون الكواكب على نطاقات ) أي أجسام شبيهة بحلق يكون تحتها مساوياً لأقطار الكواكب المركوزة فيها ( تتحرك ) تلك النطاقات ( إما بنفسها أو باعتماد الكواكب عليها ) وتكون تلك النطاقات بأسرها مغرقة في كرة واحدة على أوضاع مختلفة ( وليس ذلك ) أي إثبات النطاقات والحركة عليها ( بأبعد من إثبات ( الخارج ( المركز ( ومتمميه ( المختلفي الثخن والوضع . ( ثم ) إن سلمنا أن ذلك غير جائز ، قلنا : (لم) لا يجوز أن يكون للكل من حيث هو كل ( حركة غير حركة كل واحد وتكون هي أي حركة الكل (الحركة اليومية ) الشاملة لجميع الكواكب (فيغني ) هذا الذي ذكرناه ( عن إثبات ( الفلك ( التاسع) وذلك بأن تتعلق نفس واحدة بمجموع الأفلاك الثمانية وتحركه هذه الحركة السريعة وتتعلق بكل واحد منها نفس على حدة وتحركه حركة أخرى فينتظم حال الحركات المرصودة بلا حاجة إلى فلك تاسع. وقد زاد بعضهم على ذلك وقال : لا حاجة حينئذ إلى الثامن أيضاً لجواز فرض الثوابت ودوائر البروج على ممثل زحل، فتكون الأفلاك الكلية سبعة فقط لا تسعة. قوله : على نطاقات لا يقال : الصورة النوعية المرتسمة فيما فرضتموه نطاقاً يقتضي كرويته، فيجب أن يكون كرة، وإلا يلزم اختلاف أفعال الطبيعة الواحدة في مادة واحدة، وقد تبين بطلانه لأنا نقول : هذا الاختلاف مثل اختلاف الثخن والنقر في الفلك الواحد، وهو لا يوجب خروج فعل الطبيعة عن كونه نوعاً واحداً كما مر .
Its basis—i.e., the basis of what was mentioned of the proof for the multiplicity of spheres—is that spheres absolutely cannot be pierced. Otherwise, there could be one stationary sphere, and the motion would be for the planet itself like a swimmer in water. If that is granted—i.e., the impossibility of piercing—then why is it not permissible for the planets to be on rings (nitaqat)—i.e., bodies resembling rings beneath which is equal to the diameters of the planets embedded in them—those rings moving either by themselves or by the planets' reliance on them, and those rings entirely immersed in one sphere in different positions? And that—i.e., establishing the rings and motion upon them—is not more far-fetched than establishing the eccentric (al-kharij al-markaz) and its complements (mutamimayhi) of varying thickness and position. Then, if we grant that that is not permissible, we say: why is it not permissible for the whole, as a whole, to have a motion other than the motion of each one, and that motion (i.e., the motion of the whole) be the daily motion (al-haraka al-yawmiyya) encompassing all the planets, so that this suffices for establishing the ninth sphere? That is by one soul attaching to the set of eight spheres and moving them with this swift motion, and each sphere has its own soul moving it with another motion, so the observed motions are regulated without need for a ninth sphere. Some added to this and said: there is then no need for the eighth either, because it is possible to suppose the fixed stars and the zodiacal circles on the model (mumaththil) of Saturn, so the universal spheres would be only seven, not nine. His saying: 'on rings'—it is not said: the specific form (al-sura al-naw'iyya) impressed in what you supposed as a ring necessitates its sphericity, so it must be a sphere; otherwise, there would be different actions of one nature in one matter, and its falsity has been shown. For we say: this difference is like the difference in thickness and concavity in one sphere, and it does not necessitate the action of nature leaving being one type, as has passed.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a multi-step argument and objection-reply chain. It begins by stating the basis of the proof for multiple spheres: spheres cannot be pierced (la tankhariq). If they could be pierced, one sphere would suffice, and planets would move like swimmers. Accepting non-piercing, an objection is raised: why not have planets on rings (nitaqat) moving themselves or by the planets, all immersed in one sphere? The author replies that this is no more far-fetched than eccentrics and their complements. Then a second objection: if that is impossible, why not have a single motion for the whole (the daily motion) without a ninth sphere, by attaching one soul to all eight spheres? The answer is that this suffices, eliminating the need for a ninth sphere. Some even said the eighth sphere is unnecessary if fixed stars are placed on Saturn's model, reducing spheres to seven. A marginal note addresses a potential objection: the specific form of a ring requires sphericity, so they would be spheres, causing different actions in one matter; the author replies that such differences (like thickness) do not negate unity of nature.

Key Terms
انخراق
نطاقات
الخارج المركز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think it's possible for spheres to be pierced and planets to move like swimmers in a fluid.
Correction: The passage establishes that spheres cannot be pierced, and even if they could, it would not necessitate multiple spheres; the impossibility itself is the proof for multiplicity.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the proof for the multiplicity of spheres according to this passage?
A) Observation of planetary motions.
B) The impossibility of spheres being pierced.
C) The need for a ninth sphere.
D) The existence of rings around planets.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of piercing spheres is the logical foundation for proving multiple celestial spheres, and alternative models like rings are no less complex than accepted eccentrics.

The author here defends a complex model (multiple spheres) against a seemingly simpler one (rings) by appealing to existing accepted complexity. Eliminating the Ninth Sphere and Reducing to Seven
Objection to ninth sphere and reduction to seven

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars argued that the daily motion could be explained without a ninth sphere by positing a single soul moving all eight spheres, and how some even reduced the number of spheres to seven.

Core Idea
A single soul could move all spheres, eliminating the need for a ninth sphere.

After addressing the ring objection, the passage moves to a more radical proposal: maybe the entire set of eight spheres has its own motion (the daily rotation) governed by a single soul, while each sphere has its own soul for its proper motion. This would make a ninth sphere unnecessary. Some went further, suggesting the eighth sphere could be eliminated by placing the fixed stars on Saturn's sphere, reducing the count to seven. The passage ends with a technical reply about the nature of rings not breaking the unity of nature.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the second objection and its solution
The objector asks: why not give the whole system a motion (daily) different from individual motions? The author answers by positing a single soul for the whole and separate souls for each sphere.
This is a philosophical solution based on souls.
2
Understand the further reduction
Some said the eighth sphere is also unnecessary if the fixed stars are on Saturn's model.
This reduces spheres to seven.
3
Analyze the final reply about rings
A critic says the specific form of a ring requires it to be a sphere, leading to different actions in one matter. The author replies that such differences (like thickness) don't violate unity of nature.
This ties back to the ring objection from earlier.
4
Synthesize the argumentative moves
See how the passage progresses from necessary piercing to alternative models, and how each is refuted or absorbed.

مبناه ) أي مبنى ما ذكر من الدليل على تعدد الأفلاك هو ( أن الأفلاك لا تنخرق ( أصلاً ) وإلا جاز أن يكون هناك فلك واحد ساكن، ويكون ( الحركة للكوكب نفسه كالسابح في الماء، وإن سلم ذلك) أي امتناع الانخراق ( فلم لا يجوز أن تكون الكواكب على نطاقات ) أي أجسام شبيهة بحلق يكون تحتها مساوياً لأقطار الكواكب المركوزة فيها ( تتحرك ) تلك النطاقات ( إما بنفسها أو باعتماد الكواكب عليها ) وتكون تلك النطاقات بأسرها مغرقة في كرة واحدة على أوضاع مختلفة ( وليس ذلك ) أي إثبات النطاقات والحركة عليها ( بأبعد من إثبات ( الخارج ( المركز ( ومتمميه ( المختلفي الثخن والوضع . ( ثم ) إن سلمنا أن ذلك غير جائز ، قلنا : (لم) لا يجوز أن يكون للكل من حيث هو كل ( حركة غير حركة كل واحد وتكون هي أي حركة الكل (الحركة اليومية ) الشاملة لجميع الكواكب (فيغني ) هذا الذي ذكرناه ( عن إثبات ( الفلك ( التاسع) وذلك بأن تتعلق نفس واحدة بمجموع الأفلاك الثمانية وتحركه هذه الحركة السريعة وتتعلق بكل واحد منها نفس على حدة وتحركه حركة أخرى فينتظم حال الحركات المرصودة بلا حاجة إلى فلك تاسع. وقد زاد بعضهم على ذلك وقال : لا حاجة حينئذ إلى الثامن أيضاً لجواز فرض الثوابت ودوائر البروج على ممثل زحل، فتكون الأفلاك الكلية سبعة فقط لا تسعة. قوله : على نطاقات لا يقال : الصورة النوعية المرتسمة فيما فرضتموه نطاقاً يقتضي كرويته، فيجب أن يكون كرة، وإلا يلزم اختلاف أفعال الطبيعة الواحدة في مادة واحدة، وقد تبين بطلانه لأنا نقول : هذا الاختلاف مثل اختلاف الثخن والنقر في الفلك الواحد، وهو لا يوجب خروج فعل الطبيعة عن كونه نوعاً واحداً كما مر .
Its basis—i.e., the basis of what was mentioned of the proof for the multiplicity of spheres—is that spheres absolutely cannot be pierced. Otherwise, there could be one stationary sphere, and the motion would be for the planet itself like a swimmer in water. If that is granted—i.e., the impossibility of piercing—then why is it not permissible for the planets to be on rings (nitaqat)—i.e., bodies resembling rings beneath which is equal to the diameters of the planets embedded in them—those rings moving either by themselves or by the planets' reliance on them, and those rings entirely immersed in one sphere in different positions? And that—i.e., establishing the rings and motion upon them—is not more far-fetched than establishing the eccentric (al-kharij al-markaz) and its complements (mutamimayhi) of varying thickness and position. Then, if we grant that that is not permissible, we say: why is it not permissible for the whole, as a whole, to have a motion other than the motion of each one, and that motion (i.e., the motion of the whole) be the daily motion (al-haraka al-yawmiyya) encompassing all the planets, so that this suffices for establishing the ninth sphere? That is by one soul attaching to the set of eight spheres and moving them with this swift motion, and each sphere has its own soul moving it with another motion, so the observed motions are regulated without need for a ninth sphere. Some added to this and said: there is then no need for the eighth either, because it is possible to suppose the fixed stars and the zodiacal circles on the model (mumaththil) of Saturn, so the universal spheres would be only seven, not nine. His saying: 'on rings'—it is not said: the specific form (al-sura al-naw'iyya) impressed in what you supposed as a ring necessitates its sphericity, so it must be a sphere; otherwise, there would be different actions of one nature in one matter, and its falsity has been shown. For we say: this difference is like the difference in thickness and concavity in one sphere, and it does not necessitate the action of nature leaving being one type, as has passed.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a multi-step argument and objection-reply chain. It begins by stating the basis of the proof for multiple spheres: spheres cannot be pierced (la tankhariq). If they could be pierced, one sphere would suffice, and planets would move like swimmers. Accepting non-piercing, an objection is raised: why not have planets on rings (nitaqat) moving themselves or by the planets, all immersed in one sphere? The author replies that this is no more far-fetched than eccentrics and their complements. Then a second objection: if that is impossible, why not have a single motion for the whole (the daily motion) without a ninth sphere, by attaching one soul to all eight spheres? The answer is that this suffices, eliminating the need for a ninth sphere. Some even said the eighth sphere is unnecessary if fixed stars are placed on Saturn's model, reducing spheres to seven. A marginal note addresses a potential objection: the specific form of a ring requires sphericity, so they would be spheres, causing different actions in one matter; the author replies that such differences (like thickness) do not negate unity of nature.

ممثل زحل
الصورة النوعية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that a ninth sphere is absolutely necessary to explain the daily motion of the fixed stars.
Correction: The passage shows that the daily motion can be attributed to a single soul moving all eight spheres, eliminating the need for a ninth sphere.

Checkpoint
What replaces the ninth sphere according to the main answer in this passage?
A) A larger sphere containing all others.
B) A single soul moving all eight spheres.
C) The eccentric spheres.
D) The rings (nitaqat).

Key Takeaway
The daily motion can be explained by a single soul moving all eight spheres, and further reductions could eliminate even the eighth sphere, showing the flexibility of medieval astronomical models.

Do Fixed Stars Require Separate Spheres?
Raises objection that fixed stars could each be on a sphere, multiplying spheres infinitely.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Sanusi rebuts the objection that fixed stars could each be on separate spheres, showing why constancy of relative positions does not necessitate a single sphere.

Core Idea
Constant star positions can come from synchronized spheres, not just one sphere.

Al-Sanusi anticipates a powerful objection: if we grant his previous reasoning, why couldn't each fixed star have its own sphere? The expected answer is that star positions stay fixed relative to each other, proving one sphere. But al-Sanusi shows this constancy could come from multiple spheres moving in perfect unison. This lesson unpacks that subtle counter-argument and its astronomical mechanism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for rhythm, then the translation. Notice the objection and the expected response.
2
Identify the objection and expected answer
The objector asks: why can't each fixed star have its own sphere? The expected answer is that star positions remain constant, proving one sphere. Locate these in the text.
The key phrase is 'بقاء نسبها' (constancy of relative positions).
3
Understand al-Sanusi's counter
Al-Sanusi argues that constancy could arise from multiple spheres moving in perfect synchrony. Then follow the marginal note about Saturn's model to see how the mechanism works.
The marginal note clarifies how the fixed stars could be on Saturn's model without contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) لنا أن نقول بعد تسليم ما تقدم: (لم لا يجوز أن تكون الثوابت كل واحد منها على فلك فيتضاعف عدد الأفلاك على ما ذكروه أضعافاً مضاعفة (و) قولهم : (بقاء نسبها أي نسب بعض الثوابت إلى بعض في القرب والبعد والمحاذاة يدل على أنها مرتكزة في كرة واحدة ( لا يصلح للتعويل لجواز اتفاقها أي اتفاق تلك الأفلاك المتعددة التي عليها الثوابت ( في الحركة ) سرعةً وبطاً وجهة، فلا يتغير بتلك الحركات نسبها وأوضاعها. قوله : ( لجواز فرض الثوابت إلخ قد يتوهم أنه على ذلك التقدير لا ينقل الثوابت ولا دوائر البروج على ممثل زحل، لكن انتقاله حاصل بأن منطقة حركة الكل مقاطعة لمنطقة ممثل زحل التي هي منطقة البروج بعينها على نقطتين، فإذا جعل مبدأ القسمة أحد المتقاطعين لم يلزم محذور، والمتقاطع يكون محركاً بالحركة السريعة ورد الحركة البطيئة .
And we may say after granting what has preceded: why is it not permissible for the fixed stars, each one of them, to be on a sphere, so that the number of spheres multiplies manifold as they have mentioned? And their saying: 'the constancy of their relative positions—i.e., the proportions of some fixed stars to others in proximity, distance, and alignment—indicates that they are embedded in one sphere' is not reliable, because it is possible for those multiple spheres on which the fixed stars are to agree in motion—speed, slowness, and direction—so their relative positions and configurations do not change due to those motions. His saying: 'regarding the permissibility of supposing the fixed stars, etc.'—one might imagine that on that supposition the fixed stars and the zodiacal circles are not transferred onto the model of Saturn, but their transfer is achieved because the plane of the motion of the whole intersects the plane of the model of Saturn, which is the zodiacal plane itself, at two points. So if one makes the starting point of division one of the two intersection points, no absurdity follows, and the intersection is moved by the swift motion and responds to the slow motion.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector argues: if we accept the previous reasoning, why can't each fixed star have its own sphere, multiplying spheres infinitely? The answer they anticipate is that the fixed stars' relative positions remain constant, proving they are on one sphere. But the author counters that this constancy could arise from those multiple spheres moving in perfect agreement (same speed, slowness, direction), so relative positions wouldn't change. The marginal note further explains the mechanism: the fixed stars and zodiacal circles can be placed on Saturn's model (mumaththil Zuhal). The motion of the whole (the daily motion) intersects the zodiacal plane at two points. By taking one intersection as the starting point, no problem arises, and the intersection is moved by the swift motion and responds to the slow motion. This allows for the fixed stars to be on Saturn's model without contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Constancy of relative positions proves that fixed stars are embedded in a single sphere.
Correction: The constancy could also result from multiple spheres moving in perfect agreement (same speed, slowness, direction).

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The constancy of star positions does not logically require a single sphere; synchronized multiple spheres explain it equally well.

Objection on Fixed Stars Below Planets and the Eclipse Argument
Raises objection and gives partial response using eclipse limitation and imperceptibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that fixed stars may be below planets does not undermine the celestial order, because eclipse evidence is limited and often imperceptible.

Core Idea
Eclipses only prove order for stars in the planetary plane, not all stars.

This lesson addresses a direct challenge to the traditional arrangement of celestial spheres. The objector suggests that some fixed stars might be beneath the planets, invalidating the order. The response shows that eclipses—the main evidence—only apply to stars in the plane of planetary orbits and even then are often too subtle to be observed.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objector asks why fixed stars cannot be on spheres below the planets, which would destroy the claimed order.
Note that this is a hypothetical objection, not a confirmed observation.
2
Identify the response
The author responds that the report of eclipses is not granted, or if granted, only for fixed stars that are in the planetary orbits.
This limits the scope of the evidence.
3
Understand the limitation near the poles
For fixed stars near the poles, there are no eclipses, so we cannot tell if they are above or below planets.
4
Grasp the imperceptibility argument
Even for stars that are eclipsed, the eclipse may be invisible because the planet's light overwhelms the star's dimming.
Compare to a moon-sun eclipse that is invisible when the moon covers only a small portion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لم لا يجوز أن يكون بعضها أي بعض الثوابت على أفلاك ) تحت الأفلاك السيارة ) فلا يصح ما ذكروه من الترتيب وحكاية الكسف ) أي كسف السيارات للثوابت على ما ذكروه غير مسلم و ( إن سلم ففيما يقع ) من الثوابت ( في مداراتها ) أي محاذياً لمدارات السيارات حتى يتصور كونها كاسفة لها حاجبة لنا عن رؤيتها فيعلم كون السيارات تحتها فكيف السبيل إلى الجزم في غيرها أي في الثوابت القريبة من القطبين، إذ لا هناك كسف فلا يعلم أنها تجت السيارات أو فوقها ولا يمكن التمسك في ذلك باختلاف المنظر وعدمه. أما بالقياس إلى العلوية فظاهر وأما بالقياس إلى غيرها من الثوابت ما ليست مرصودة لصغرها، فلا يعلم أن لها اختلاف منظر أو لا . قوله : ( وحكاية الكسف إلخ ) فإنه إذا كسف القمر الشمس بقدر ما يكون مثل قطر الزهرة أو قطر عطارد لا يظهر كسوفها للأبصار مع أن الكاسف في غاية الإظلام، فكيف والكاسف نير، فالثوابت تضمحل أنوار السيارات . قوله : ( لجواز فرض الثوابت ودوائر البروج على ممثل (حل اعلم أن ممثل زحل هو مجموع المتمم الحاوي لحامل زحل والمتمم المحوي لهذا الحامل أيضاً، وأما حامل زحل فهو الفلك الخارج المركز لتدوير زحل على ما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى، وإنما جاز فرض الكواكب الثابتة على ممثل زحل لأنهم وجدوا حركة ممثل رحل مثل حركة فلك الثوابت، بحيث يتخيل أن هذا الممثل يتحرك بحركة فلك الثوابت، وسيجيء تفصيله فإن قيل : يلزم من ذلك الفرض أن ينكسف زحل ببعض الثوابت المسامتة له وبالعكس أيضاً، لكن الحس يكذبه، قلنا: حكاية الكسف ممنوعة كما ذكره إذ الحس لا يقدر أن يميز الكاسف عن المنكسف هناك، فإن الظاهر أن أحد الكوكبين مثل الآخر في الشكل واللون، وإن لم يكن في المقدار، لكن عظم المقدار وصغره لا يفيد في تميز أحدهما عن الآخر في الحس عند كونهما متحاذيين في الحس أيضاً.
Then, why is it not permissible for some of the fixed stars—i.e., some of them—to be on spheres beneath the planetary spheres? So what they mentioned of the arrangement and the report of eclipses (kusuf)—i.e., the eclipses of the planets by the fixed stars as they mentioned—is not granted, and if it is granted, then only for those fixed stars that fall in their orbits (i.e., aligned with planetary orbits) so that they can be conceived as eclipsing them and hiding them from us, thus knowing that the planets are beneath them. So how can one be certain regarding others, i.e., the fixed stars near the poles? For there is no eclipse there, so it is not known whether they are below or above the planets, nor can one rely on the existence or absence of parallax (ikhtilaf al-manzar). As for comparison to the superior planets, it is obvious; as for comparison to other fixed stars that are not observed due to their smallness, one does not know whether they have parallax or not. His saying: 'the report of eclipses, etc.'—for if the moon eclipses the sun by an amount equal to the diameter of Venus or Mercury, its eclipse does not appear to the eyes, even though the eclipsing body (the moon) is in extreme darkness; how then when the eclipsing body is luminous? So the fixed stars diminish the lights of the planets. His saying: 'regarding the permissibility of supposing the fixed stars and zodiacal circles on the model of Saturn'—know that the model of Saturn (mumaththil Zuhal) is the sum of the complement (mutammim) containing the carrier (hamil) of Saturn and the complement contained for this carrier also. As for the carrier of Saturn, it is the eccentric sphere (al-falak al-kharij al-markaz) for the epicycle (tadwir) of Saturn, as will come if God wills. It is permissible to suppose the fixed stars on the model of Saturn because they found the motion of the model of Saturn similar to the motion of the sphere of fixed stars, such that one imagines this model moves with the motion of the sphere of fixed stars, and details will come. If it is said: this supposition entails that Saturn would be eclipsed by some fixed stars aligned with it and vice versa, but observation denies it; we say: the report of eclipses is denied as he mentioned, because the senses cannot distinguish the eclipsing from the eclipsed there; for it appears that one of the two planets is like the other in shape and color, even if not in magnitude, but largeness and smallness of magnitude do not help distinguish one from the other by sense when they are aligned in sense as well.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage continues the objection-answer sequence. The objector asks: why cannot some fixed stars be below planetary spheres, disproving the claimed order? The author replies that the evidence from eclipses (where a planet hides a star) is unreliable because eclipses are only observable for stars in the planetary orbits, not for those near the poles. Moreover, even for eclipses, they are imperceptible: if the moon eclipses the sun by the diameter of Venus or Mercury, it is not seen, let alone when the eclipsing body is bright. So fixed stars actually diminish the planets' light. The marginal note about the model of Saturn explains that fixed stars can be placed on Saturn's model because their motions match. An objection that this would cause Saturn to be eclipsed by fixed stars is answered: such eclipses are imperceptible because the senses cannot distinguish the eclipsing from the eclipsed when they are similar in appearance.

Key Terms
كسف
اختلاف المنظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That eclipses clearly prove that all fixed stars are above the planets.
Correction: Eclipses only prove order for stars in the planetary plane, and even then they are often imperceptible.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why can't eclipses prove the order of all fixed stars relative to planets?
A) Because fixed stars are too bright.
B) Because eclipses only occur for stars in the planetary orbits, not near the poles.
C) Because planets never eclipse fixed stars.
D) Because the senses are always deceived.

Key Takeaway
Eclipse evidence for celestial order is limited to stars in the plane of planetary orbits and is often imperceptible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on your senses and reason to navigate the world. This passage shows that even clear astronomical evidence can be unreliable or incomplete. Where in your own life have you assumed that your observations give you complete knowledge, when in fact you were only seeing part of the picture? How can you cultivate humility about your own perception and turn instead to divine revelation for certainty?
?
The author shows that eclipse reports are only valid for some stars, not all. You may have built your faith on partial evidence or popular arguments. Is there an area where you have accepted a theological claim based on limited evidence without deeper verification? What would it mean for you to seek a more thorough understanding, even if it requires effort?
?
If the moon’s eclipse of the sun by a small amount is imperceptible, how much more so when a luminous star covers a planet? This is an a fortiori argument. Consider your own sins: you may think small transgressions are imperceptible to God or have no effect. How does this passage challenge you to take even minor spiritual failings seriously, knowing that what is small in your eyes may be significant in the sight of God?
