Proof that Celestial Motions Are Voluntary
Al-Jurjani argues that celestial motions are not natural and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why celestial motions cannot be natural and must be voluntary, and how al-Jurjani refines the argument against an objection.

Core Idea
Circular motion's simultaneous seeking and abandoning of a position proves it requires will, not nature.

Al-Jurjani begins the investigation of celestial souls by arguing that their motions are voluntary. He uses a clever argument from the nature of circular motion: if it were natural, the same position would be both desired and shunned, which is impossible. He also addresses an objection and strengthens the argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
The passage is part of the third observation on immaterial souls. The first purpose is on celestial souls, which are immaterial because their motions are voluntary.
This sets up the need to prove the motions are voluntary.
2
Learn the classification of motions
Al-Jurjani states that all essential motions are either natural, forced, or voluntary. To show celestial motions are voluntary, he first eliminates natural and forced.
This is a standard division in kalam.
3
Grasp the argument against natural motion
In circular motion, every position the mover reaches is both sought (since it moves toward it) and abandoned (since it leaves it). If it were natural, the same position would be naturally desired and naturally abandoned, a contradiction.
This is the core proof.
4
See the objection and refinement
An objection says that leaving a position is not identical to seeking it. Al-Jurjani refines the argument: the mover seeks a specific position and then abandons it, which requires perception and will.
The refined argument is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثالث في مباحث النفوس المجردة وأحكامها شرع في بيانها بعد الفراغ من مباحث الأجسام وعوارضها ( وفيه مقاصد ) أربعة . ( المقصد الأول: في النفوس الفلكية ) في النفوس الفلكية وهي مجردة عن المادة وتوابعها ( لأن حركات الأفلاك ) إرادية فلها نفوس مجردة . أما الأول ) وهو كون حركاتها إرادية ( فلأنها إما طبيعية أو قسرية أو إرادية ) لما مر من أن أقسام الحركة الذاتية منحصرة فيها ( والأولان باطلان ) فتعين الثالث ( أما كونها طبيعية فلأن الحركة الدورية كل ما وضع فيها فهو مطلوب ومتروك فلو كان ذلك التحرك الدوري (مقتضى (الطبيعة) ومستنداً إليها (لكان الشيء الواحد ) وهو الوضع المخصوص ) مطلوباً بالطبع ومتروكاً بالطبع وإنه محال) وقد وجه هذا الدليل بأن كل وضع يتوجه إليه المتحرك بالاستدارة يكون ترك ذلك الوضع هو عين التوجه إليه، فيكون المهروب عنه بالطبع بعينه مطلوباً بالطبع في حالة واحدة بل يكون الهرب عن الشيء عين طلبه وأنه محال بديهة. ورد عليه بأنه ترك وضع ليس توجهاً إليه بعينه لانعدامه بتركه بل غايته أنه توجه إلى مثله فلا يكون المتروك نفس المطلوب فالأولى أن يوجه بأن المتحرك بحركته المستديرة يطلب وضعاً ثم يتركه ومثله لا يتصور من فاقد الإرادة لأن طلب الشيء المعين وتركه لا يكون إلا باختلاف الأغراض الموقوفة على الشعور والإرادة
The third observation: on the investigation of immaterial souls and their properties. He began explaining them after finishing from the investigation of bodies and their accidents. And it contains four purposes. The first purpose: on the celestial souls. The celestial souls are immaterial from matter and its attachments, because the motions of the celestial spheres are voluntary, so they have immaterial souls. As for the first point, which is that their motions are voluntary, it is because they are either natural, or forced, or voluntary, as has passed that the divisions of essential motion are restricted to these. And the first two are false, so the third is determined. As for their being natural, because in circular motion, every position it occupies is simultaneously sought and abandoned. If that circular motion were a requirement of nature and based upon it, then one single thing—namely the particular position—would be naturally desired and naturally abandoned, which is impossible. This proof has been expressed as: every position the mover approaches by rotation, the leaving of that position is exactly the approaching to it, so the naturally shunned is identical to the naturally desired in one state; rather, fleeing from something is exactly seeking it, and that is obviously impossible. And it was refuted that leaving a position is not approaching it exactly, because it ceases to exist upon leaving, but at most it is an approach to a similar one, so the abandoned is not the same as the sought. So the better way is to express it as: the mover by its circular motion seeks a position and then abandons it, and such is inconceivable from one lacking will, because seeking a particular thing and abandoning it only occurs due to differing purposes dependent on perception and will.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage begins the third observation on immaterial souls. Al-Jurjani states that the first purpose concerns celestial souls, which are immaterial because their motions are voluntary. He then presents the classification of motions into natural, forced, and voluntary. To prove that celestial motions are voluntary, he first shows they are not natural. The argument: in circular motion, every position is both sought and abandoned. If it were natural, the same position would be both naturally desired and naturally abandoned—a contradiction. An objection that abandoning a position is not identical to seeking it is noted, but Al-Jurjani favors a stronger formulation: the circular mover seeks a position and then abandons it, which requires will, as such alternation of seeking and abandoning depends on changing purposes that only a voluntary agent possesses.

Key Terms
نفوس مجردة (immaterial souls)
حركات إرادية (voluntary motions)
حركة طبيعية (natural motion)
وضع مخصوص (particular position)
شعور (perception)
إرادة (will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection refutes the argument, showing that circular motion could be natural after all.
Correction: Al-Jurjani does not accept the objection as a refutation; instead, he improves the argument to make it even clearer that voluntary agency is required.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why cannot circular motion be natural?
A) Because nature cannot produce circular motion.
B) Because the same position would be both naturally desired and abandoned, a contradiction.
C) Because celestial spheres have no nature.
D) Because forced motion is more plausible.

Key Takeaway
Celestial motions are voluntary because circular motion involves seeking and abandoning particular positions, which requires perception and will, not mere nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Jurjani argues that circular motion requires will because it involves seeking and then abandoning a particular position. Reflect on your own life: are there positions, goals, or attachments that you both seek and abandon repeatedly? What does this reveal about your intentions? Are you living with a clear purpose or just going in circles? Commit today to identify one such cycle and turn it into a deliberate, purposeful choice.
?
The proof shows that even the celestial spheres cannot act without perception and will. Consider your daily actions: how many of them are driven by mere habit, nature, or external pressure rather than conscious will and sincere intention toward Allah? Pick one routine action (e.g., praying, eating, working) and decide to perform it with renewed awareness and intention, as if it were a voluntary act of worship.
?
If the same thing cannot be both naturally desired and naturally shunned, what about your heart? Are there contradictions in your desires—saying you love Allah yet sinning, claiming to seek the Hereafter while clinging to this world? Confront one such contradiction today and take a concrete step to resolve it in favor of what pleases Allah.

Proof that Celestial Motions Are Not Forced
Al-Jurjani gives two reasons why celestial motions are not forced.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Jurjani rejects forced motion for celestial spheres and the two arguments he uses.

Core Idea
Celestial motions cannot be forced because there is no nature to oppose and observations show diversity.

Al-Jurjani continues the investigation into celestial motions by examining the possibility that they are forced. He provides two compelling arguments: one based on the absence of natural inclination, and another based on the observed diversity of motions. This lesson unpacks these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two distinct arguments introduced by 'فلما تقدم' and 'وأيضاً'.
2
Identify the two arguments
The passage presents two reasons why motions cannot be forced: (1) absence of natural inclination, (2) observed diversity contradicts forced uniformity. Locate each and understand the reasoning.
3
Reflect on forced motion implications
Ask yourself: if celestial motions were forced, what would we expect to see? How does observation contradict that? This helps solidify the argument.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما كونها قسرية فلما تقدم أن القسر إنما يكون على خلاف الطبع وذلك لأنه تقدم في مباحث الاعتمادات ) هو بمعناه أعني ) أن عديم الميل الطبيعي لا يتحرك قسرا ( وهاهنا لا طبع فلا قسر، وأيضاً فلو كان تحرك الأفلاك على الاستدارة ) بالقسر لكان على موافقة القاسر فوجب تشابه (حركاتها في الجهة والسرعة والبطء وتوافقها في المناطق والأقطاب إذ لا يتصور هناك قسر إلا من بعضها لبعض لكن حركاتها كما شهدت به الأرصاد ليست متشابهة ولا متوافقة . ( وأما الثاني ) وهو أنه إذا كانت حركاتها إرادية كانت لها نفوس مجردة ( فلان إرادتها ( المتعلقة بحركاتها ( ليست) ناشئة عن تخيل محض من قوة جسمانية تدرك أموراً جزئية ) وإلا امتنع دوامها ) أي دوام ما الحركات الفلكية على نظام واحد دهر (الداهرين أي أزلاً وأبداً لا يختلف ولا يتغير لا في الجهة ولا في السرعة ألا ترى أن الحركات الحيوانية المستندة إلى الإدراكات الجزئية تختلف وتنقطع ( فهي ) أي إرادتها التي تترتب عليها الحركات السرمدية على وتيرة واحدة إذن) ناشئة عن تعقل كلي ( يندرج فيه أمور غير متناهية ( ( ومحل التعقل الكلي مجرد لما سيأتي في النفوس الإنسانية برهانه
As for their being forced: because it has preceded that force is contrary to nature, and that is because it has preceded in the investigations of inclinations—by its meaning I mean—that which has no natural inclination cannot be moved by force, and here there is no nature, so there is no force. Also, if the celestial spheres moved in rotation by force, they would have to conform to the coercer, so their motions would necessarily be similar in direction, speed, and slowness, and they would correspond in their regions and poles, since force there is conceivable only from some of them upon others. But their motions, as verified by observations, are neither similar nor corresponding. As for the second point, which is that if their motions are voluntary, then they have immaterial souls: because their will related to their motions does not arise from mere imagination from a corporeal power that perceives particular things; otherwise their perpetuity would be impossible—that is, the perpetuity of the celestial motions upon one system forever, eternally and perpetually, not differing or changing, not in direction nor in speed. Do you not see that animal motions based on particular perceptions differ and cease? So that will, upon which eternal motions in one uniform manner are based, must arise from a universal intellection that encompasses infinite things. And the locus of universal intellection is immaterial, as its proof will come in the human souls.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage continues the proof that celestial motions are voluntary. First, Al-Jurjani argues they are not forced: force requires a natural inclination to be contrary to, but celestial spheres have no natural inclination (as shown by the failure of the natural motion hypothesis). Moreover, if they were forced, all motions would be similar due to a single coercer, but observations show diversity in direction and speed. Thus forced motion is false, leaving voluntary motion. Second, he argues that voluntary motion of such constancy and perpetuity cannot arise from a corporeal imagination, which produces variable and intermittent motions. Instead, it must proceed from a universal intellection (ta'aqqul kullī) encompassing infinite particulars, and such intellection requires an immaterial subject (a soul). This prepares for the later proof concerning human souls.

Key Terms
قسر (force)
ميل طبيعي (natural inclination)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Al-Jurjani argue that celestial motions cannot be forced?
A) Because they are too fast.
B) Because they lack natural inclination and observations show diversity.
C) Because force only applies to earthly objects.
D) Because angels move them directly.

Key Takeaway
Celestial motions are not forced because they have no natural inclination to be contrary to, and their observed diversity contradicts the uniformity required by force.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever act religiously out of compulsion or social pressure rather than from your own nature? Reflect on one area of your life where you feel 'forced' in your faith. What would it take to make that action flow naturally from your fitrah, like the harmonious motion of the heavens?
?
The celestial spheres move in diversity yet without force. Do you accept the diversity in Allah's creation and in people as a sign of wisdom, or do you try to impose uniformity in your expectations of others? What would change if you saw diversity as deliberate rather than forced?
?
Al-Jurjani argues that something without nature cannot be forced. Your soul has a natural inclination toward good (fitrah). When you sin, you are acting against that nature. What force is making you do so? Identify one specific sin and trace it back to an external pressure or internal desire. How can you return to your natural state?

Proof that Celestial Souls Are Immaterial
Al-Jurjani argues that voluntary celestial motions imply immaterial souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Jurjani deduces that celestial motions must arise from an immaterial soul that possesses universal intellection.

Core Idea
Uniform perpetual motion cannot come from imagination but requires an immaterial soul with universal intellection.

Having established that celestial motions are voluntary, Al-Jurjani now asks what kind of will produces such uniform perpetual motion. He argues it cannot be based on corporeal imagination, which yields variable and intermittent motions, but must be based on universal intellection, which requires an immaterial subject. This lesson traces his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Notice the key contrast between imagination and universal intellection.
The phrase 'ألا ترى أن الحركات الحيوانية...' signals an analogy.
2
Identify the argument structure
The passage argues: (a) celestial motions are uniform and perpetual, (b) animal motions from imagination are variable and cease, (c) therefore the will causing celestial motions must arise from universal intellection, which requires an immaterial soul. Trace this chain.
3
Understand why universal intellection is immaterial
Universal intellection deals with infinite particulars and cannot be limited by a corporeal substrate. Al-Jurjani points to a later proof concerning human souls. For now, accept the principle.
This will be further justified in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما كونها قسرية فلما تقدم أن القسر إنما يكون على خلاف الطبع وذلك لأنه تقدم في مباحث الاعتمادات ) هو بمعناه أعني ) أن عديم الميل الطبيعي لا يتحرك قسرا ( وهاهنا لا طبع فلا قسر، وأيضاً فلو كان تحرك الأفلاك على الاستدارة ) بالقسر لكان على موافقة القاسر فوجب تشابه (حركاتها في الجهة والسرعة والبطء وتوافقها في المناطق والأقطاب إذ لا يتصور هناك قسر إلا من بعضها لبعض لكن حركاتها كما شهدت به الأرصاد ليست متشابهة ولا متوافقة . ( وأما الثاني ) وهو أنه إذا كانت حركاتها إرادية كانت لها نفوس مجردة ( فلان إرادتها ( المتعلقة بحركاتها ( ليست) ناشئة عن تخيل محض من قوة جسمانية تدرك أموراً جزئية ) وإلا امتنع دوامها ) أي دوام ما الحركات الفلكية على نظام واحد دهر (الداهرين أي أزلاً وأبداً لا يختلف ولا يتغير لا في الجهة ولا في السرعة ألا ترى أن الحركات الحيوانية المستندة إلى الإدراكات الجزئية تختلف وتنقطع ( فهي ) أي إرادتها التي تترتب عليها الحركات السرمدية على وتيرة واحدة إذن) ناشئة عن تعقل كلي ( يندرج فيه أمور غير متناهية ( ( ومحل التعقل الكلي مجرد لما سيأتي في النفوس الإنسانية برهانه
As for their being forced: because it has preceded that force is contrary to nature, and that is because it has preceded in the investigations of inclinations—by its meaning I mean—that which has no natural inclination cannot be moved by force, and here there is no nature, so there is no force. Also, if the celestial spheres moved in rotation by force, they would have to conform to the coercer, so their motions would necessarily be similar in direction, speed, and slowness, and they would correspond in their regions and poles, since force there is conceivable only from some of them upon others. But their motions, as verified by observations, are neither similar nor corresponding. As for the second point, which is that if their motions are voluntary, then they have immaterial souls: because their will related to their motions does not arise from mere imagination from a corporeal power that perceives particular things; otherwise their perpetuity would be impossible—that is, the perpetuity of the celestial motions upon one system forever, eternally and perpetually, not differing or changing, not in direction nor in speed. Do you not see that animal motions based on particular perceptions differ and cease? So that will, upon which eternal motions in one uniform manner are based, must arise from a universal intellection that encompasses infinite things. And the locus of universal intellection is immaterial, as its proof will come in the human souls.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage continues the proof that celestial motions are voluntary. First, Al-Jurjani argues they are not forced: force requires a natural inclination to be contrary to, but celestial spheres have no natural inclination (as shown by the failure of the natural motion hypothesis). Moreover, if they were forced, all motions would be similar due to a single coercer, but observations show diversity in direction and speed. Thus forced motion is false, leaving voluntary motion. Second, he argues that voluntary motion of such constancy and perpetuity cannot arise from a corporeal imagination, which produces variable and intermittent motions. Instead, it must proceed from a universal intellection (ta'aqqul kullī) encompassing infinite particulars, and such intellection requires an immaterial subject (a soul). This prepares for the later proof concerning human souls.

Key Terms
تعقل كلي (universal intellection)
نفس مجردة (immaterial soul)
تخيل (imagination)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Perpetual motion alone proves immateriality
Correction: The argument specifically ties immateriality to uniform perpetuity from a universal cause, not just perpetuity.

Checkpoint

A) Earthly motions

C) Angelic motions

Key Takeaway
The uniformity and perpetuity of celestial motions reveal that their will arises from an immaterial soul with universal intellection, not from corporeal imagination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The celestial spheres move with perfect uniformity and perpetuity because their will arises from universal intellection. Your own will is often inconsistent and driven by particular desires. As you examine your life today, where is your will being shaped by mere imagination and transitory impulses? Will you commit to grounding your intentions in a higher, universal truth that grants consistency?
?
Al-Jurjani argues that animal motions vary and cease because they rely on particular perceptions. In what areas of your spiritual life have you allowed your actions to become erratic, responding only to immediate circumstances rather than an unwavering principle? How can you train your soul to act with the uniformity of the celestial spheres?
?
The passage reminds you that the universe itself obeys a single, eternal will. Yet your own obedience to your Creator is often interrupted by negligence and forgetfulness. If the celestial bodies never tire in their worship (as implied by their uniform motion), what does your inconsistency reveal about the state of your soul? What one change will you make today to align your will with that eternal order?

Two Corollaries on Celestial Souls
Al-Jurjani derives two implications of celestial souls being immaterial and rational.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why celestial souls, despite being rational, need corporeal powers for particular motions and why they lack senses, desire, and anger.

Core Idea
Even perfect intelligences require particular powers for motion; they have no need for imperfect faculties.

Al-Jurjani has established that celestial spheres have immaterial, rational souls. Now he draws two important implications. First, since these souls engage in motion, they must have a power that can specify which particular motion to perform—something universal reason cannot do alone. Second, because celestial beings are perfect, they have no need for the lower faculties like sense, desire, or anger. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the two corollaries introduced with 'al-awwal' and 'al-thani'.
The second corollary is cut off in the source, but the point is clear.
2
Identify the two corollaries
The first corollary states that celestial souls have corporeal powers (impressed souls) for particular motions. The second states they lack external senses, desire, and anger.
3
Understand why rational power alone is insufficient
Universal intellection relates equally to all particulars. To specify one motion over another, a particular perception and will are needed, which requires a corporeal power like imagination.
This is the key argument for the first corollary.
4
Understand why lower faculties are absent
Senses, desire, and anger are for seeking benefit and repelling harm. Celestial souls, being perfect, have no such needs, so they lack these faculties.
This completes the second corollary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هناك تفريعان على القول بأن للأفلاك نفوساً مجردة وأنها أحياء ناطقة (الأول: لها مع القوة العقلية) التي نسبتها إليها كنسبة النفس الناطقة إلينا قوى جسمانية هي) بتخيلاتها (مبدأ للحركات الجزئية ) الصادرة عنها ( فإن التعقل الكلي لا يصلح لذلك أي لكونه مبدأ لوقوع الحركة الجزئية ) فإن نسبته إلى جميع الجزئيات سواء فلا يصلح مبدأ لتخصيص البعض بالوقوع (دون البعض ) بل لا بد في وقوعه من إرادة جزئية متفرعة من إدراك جزئي لا يتصور إلا من قوة جسمانية، وهذه القوى في الأفلاك كالخيال فينا إلا أنها سارية في جميع أجزائها بسيطة وتسمى نفوساً منطبعة . ( الثاني : ليس للأفلاك حس) من الحواس الظاهرة ) ولا شهوة ولا غضب لأن الاحتياج إليهما لجلب النفع ...
There are two corollaries based on the claim that the spheres have immaterial souls and that they are rational living beings. First: They have, along with the rational power—whose relation to them is like the relation of the rational soul to us—corporeal powers that are, by their imaginations, the principle of the particular motions emitted from them. For universal intellection is not suitable for this, that is, to be the principle of the occurrence of a particular motion, since its relation to all particulars is equal, so it is not suitable to specify some for occurrence over others. Rather, for its occurrence there must be a particular will branching from a particular perception, which is only conceivable from a corporeal power. These powers in the spheres are like imagination in us, except that they pervade all their parts simply and are called impressed souls. Second: The spheres do not have sense from the external senses, nor desire, nor anger, because the need for them is to seek benefit...
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage lists two corollaries that follow from the doctrine that celestial souls are immaterial and rational. First, although they have a rational power (universal intellection), they also require corporeal powers (imaginations) to produce particular motions, since universal intellection alone cannot specify which particular movement to make. These corporeal powers are like imagination in humans but pervade the whole sphere and are called impressed souls (nufūs munṭabi'a). Second, celestial souls lack external senses, desire, and anger, because these faculties are needed to pursue benefit and repel harm, which do not apply to celestial beings who are already perfect. The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the second corollary is clearly stated.

Key Terms
نفس منطبعة (impressed soul)
قوة عقلية (rational power)
إرادة جزئية (particular will)
إدراك جزئي (particular perception)
خيال (imagination)
شهوة (desire)
غضب (anger)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think celestial souls are purely rational and have no need for any corporeal power.
Correction: While they have a rational power, they also require corporeal powers (impressed souls) to produce particular motions, as universal intellection alone cannot specify which motion to perform.

Checkpoint
Why do celestial souls need corporeal powers (impressed souls) in addition to rational power?
A) To perceive the physical world.
B) To produce particular voluntary motions.
C) To feel pleasure and pain.
D) To communicate with each other.

Key Takeaway
Celestial souls combine universal intellectual power with corporeal imaginative powers to produce particular motions, and they lack lower faculties like senses, desire, and anger because they are perfect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your soul has both rational and imaginative powers. Are you allowing your imagination to serve your intellect in directing your actions toward God, or is it leading you astray? What specific step can you take today to align your particular perceptions with universal truths?
?
The celestial spheres lack desire and anger because they are perfect. You still have these faculties. Which desire in your life is not serving your ultimate purpose, and how will you begin to purify it this week?
?
If you cannot rely on universal principles alone to guide your particular actions, how will you ensure your daily choices are not random but informed by a higher vision? Write down one decision you need to approach with more particular intention.

The Createdness of the Rational Soul: Evidence and Disagreement
Al-Ījī presents Islamic and philosophical arguments for the soul's creation, noting their weakness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic and philosophical debates on whether the rational soul is created, and why the cited proofs are considered only probable.

Core Idea
The soul's createdness is Islamically agreed, but the evidence is only probable, not certain.

This passage from al-Ījī addresses a key theological question: is the rational soul created or eternal? While the Muslim community agrees it is created, they differ on when it occurs. The author then critically examines the proofs, showing they yield only probability, and notes a parallel debate among philosophers. This lesson explores the arguments and their limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the source text carefully, noting the structure: first the Islamic consensus, then the two opinions, then the critique, then the philosophical turn.
The passage ends mid-sentence; focus on the available arguments.
2
Identify the two Islamic opinions on timing
Find the two positions: the soul created with the body (based on Quran 23:14) and before the body (based on a hadith). Understand the evidence each side uses.
3
Understand the critique of the evidence
The author argues both proofs yield only probability (ẓann), not certainty. For the verse, it may refer only to attachment; for the hadith, it is a singular report conflicting with a definitive text.
This is a key methodological point in kalām.
4
Note the philosophical disagreement
Aristotle and his followers affirm creation, while earlier philosophers denied it. The argument for creation is introduced but incomplete.
The incomplete argument is a limitation of the source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثالث : في النفس الناطقة (في أن النفس الناطقة حادثة اتفق عليه المليون إذ لا قديم عندهم إلا الله وصفاته) عند من أثبتها زائدة على ذاته) لكنهم اختلفوا في أنها هل تحدث مع) حدوث (البدن أو قبله فقال : بعضهم تحدث معه لقوله تعالى بعد تعداد أطوار البدن ﴿ثم أنشأناه خلقاً آخر﴾ [المؤمنون: ٤١]، والمراد بهذا الإنشاء (إفاضة النفس) على البدن) وقال بعضهم : بل قبله لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : «خلق الله الأرواح قبل الأجساد بألفي عام» وغاية هذه الأدلة الظن) دون اليقين الذي هو المطلوب (أما الآية فلجواز أن يريد بقوله : ثم أنشأناه جعل النفس متعلقة به وإنما يلزم من) حدوث تعلقها لا حدوث ذاتها وأما الحديث فلأنه خبر واحد فتعارضه مقطوعة المتن مظنونة الدلالة والحديث بالعكس فلكل رجحان من وجه فيتقاومان (هذا) كما ذكرناه (و) أما (الحكماء) فإنهم قد اختلفوا في حدوثها فقال به أرسطو ومن تبعه، ومنعه من قبله وقالوا بقدمها احتج أرسطو بأنها لو قدمت فإما أن
The third objective: On the rational soul. (That the rational soul is created, the milla [religious community] agreed upon it, for they hold nothing as eternal except Allah and His attributes) for those who affirm them as additional to His essence. (But they differed over whether it occurs with) the occurrence (of the body or before it. Some said it occurs with it, due to His saying after enumerating the stages of the body: 'Then We produced it as another creation' [23:14], and what is meant by this production is the effusion of the soul upon the body. And some said rather before it, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Allah created the souls two thousand years before the bodies.' And the utmost of these evidences is probability, not certainty which is sought. As for the verse, it is possible that what He means by 'then We produced it' is making the soul attached to it, and what follows is only the occurrence of its attachment, not the occurrence of its essence. As for the hadith, it is a singular report, so a text that is definitive in meaning but probable in transmission opposes it, and the hadith is the opposite, so each has preponderance in some aspect, thus they counterbalance each other. This, as we mentioned. And as for the philosophers, they indeed differed over its occurrence: Aristotle and those who follow him affirmed it, while those before him denied it and said it is eternal. Aristotle argued that if it were eternal, then either...
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage begins the third objective on the rational soul, specifically regarding whether it is created (ḥāditha). The author states that the religious community (al-milliyūn) agrees it is created, since nothing is eternal except Allah and His attributes (for those who affirm attributes as additional). However, they differ on whether it is created with the body or before it. One opinion, based on the Quranic verse 'Then We produced it as another creation', holds that the soul is created simultaneously with the body; the other, based on a hadith saying souls were created two thousand years before bodies, holds it is prior. The author then criticizes these proofs as yielding only probability (ẓann), not certainty (yaqīn). The verse could mean only the attachment of the soul, not its essence. The hadith is a singular report (khabar wāḥid) that conflicts with a definitive-text (maqṭūʿ al-mutn) but probable in meaning, so they counterbalance. Then the author turns to philosophers: Aristotle and his followers say it is created, while earlier philosophers said it is eternal. The argument of Aristotle is introduced but cut off at the page end.

Key Terms
النفس الناطقة
حادثة
قديم
إفاضة النفس
خبر واحد
مقطوعة المتن
مظنونة الدلالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verse 'Then We produced it as another creation' definitively proves that the soul is created with the body.
Correction: The verse could mean only that the soul becomes attached to the body at that time, not that the soul's essence is created then.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main weakness of the Islamic evidence for the soul's creation?
A) It is rejected by all philosophers.
B) It provides only probability (ẓann), not certainty (yaqīn).
C) The Quranic verse is not authentic.
D) The hadith contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Islamic arguments for the soul's creation are only probable, and the philosophical debate remains unresolved in this passage.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on religious proofs for your beliefs about the soul. After reading that these proofs are only probable, do you still hold the same level of certainty? What does that say about the foundation of your conviction?
?
The author says the arguments counterbalance each other. If two pieces of evidence balance, how do you choose? Is your faith in the soul's createdness based on evidence or on trust? Examine your heart: is your belief built on certain knowledge or on following the community? Would you be shaken if someone challenged the probabilistic proofs?
?
The philosophers disagreed about the soul's eternity. You might think philosophy is irrelevant, but the issue is about your own soul's origin. Are you content to rely on probable arguments for something as fundamental as your soul's nature? How much are you willing to invest in seeking certainty about your own existence?

First Rational Proof: The Intellect as the First Creation
Argument eliminating candidates for first creation to prove it is the intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that the first emanation from God must be the intellect, based on the principle that from the One only one simple thing can proceed.

Core Idea
From the truly One, only one simple thing can directly emanate; only the intellect fits.

This lesson presents the first rational proof (al-wajh al-awwal) from the classical kalam tradition, based on the nature of divine unity. The author systematically eliminates all candidates for the first creation—body, matter, form, accident, soul—until only the intellect remains. This argument is foundational for understanding the hierarchy of creation in Islamic philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Principle
Learn the key premise: from the truly One (God) only one simple thing can proceed directly. This is the foundation of the proof.
The 'truly One' means no multiplicity in any respect.
2
Examine Why a Body Cannot Be First
See why a body is eliminated due to its composition (parts precede the whole, implying multiplicity and priority of parts).
A body is composite; therefore it cannot be the first simple emanation.
3
Eliminate Dependent Entities
Consider why accident and soul are also impossible: an accident depends on a substance, a soul depends on a body for action. Both lack independence.
Independence in existence (for accident) and independence in effect (for soul) are required.
4
Conclude with the Intellect
Recognize that the intellect alone is both simple (non-composite) and independent in existence and effect, making it the only candidate for the first emanation.
The intellect is self-subsistent and does not need a body for its essential activity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : الله تعالى واحد حقيقي لا تكثر فيه أصلاً بوجه من الوجوه فلا يصدر عنه ابتداء إلا الواحد ويمتنع أن يكون ذلك الصادر عنه جسماً لتركبه فلو صدر أولاً لزم تعدد الصادر في المرتبة الأولى ولتقدم الهيولى والصورة عليه ضرورة لأن الجزء متقدم على الكل فلو كان هو الصادر الأول لتقدم على أجزائه ، ولا يجوز أيضاً أن يكون الصادر الأول أحد جزأيه إذ لا يستقبل بالوجود دون الآخر فلا يستقل بالتأثير أيضاً والصادر الأول مستقل بالوجود والتأثير معاً ولا عرضاً إذ لا يستقل بالوجود دون الجوهر الذي هو محله فكيف يوجد قبله ولا نفساً إذ لا تستقل بالتأثير دون الجسم الذي هو آلتها فيمتنع أن يكون سبباً لما بعده ويجب ذلك فيما صدر أولاً فتعين أن يكون الصادر الأول هو العقل. تلخيصه أول صادر عنه تعالى واحد مستقل بالوجود والتأثير، وغير العقل ليس كذلك لانتفاء القيد الأول في الجسم، والثاني في الهيولى والصورة والعرض، والثالث في النفس
The first [proof]: God Almighty is truly One, having no multiplicity at all in any respect, so nothing proceeds from Him in the first instance except the one. And it is impossible that that which proceeds from Him is a body, due to its composition; for if it were the first to proceed, it would necessitate multiplicity in the first rank, and the priority of matter and form over it would be necessary, because the part precedes the whole. So if it were the first emanation, it would precede its parts. Nor is it permissible that the first emanation be one of its two parts, since it does not come into existence without the other, nor is it independent in its effect; while the first emanation is independent in both existence and effect. Nor can it be an accident, since it is not independent in existence without the substance that is its subject; how then could it exist before it? Nor can it be a soul, since it is not independent in effect without the body that is its instrument. Thus it is impossible that it be a cause for what is after it, but that is necessary for that which proceeds first. Therefore it is determined that the first emanation is the intellect. Its summary: The first emitter from Him is one, independent in existence and effect. Other than the intellect is not so, because the first condition (independence in existence) is absent in the body, the second (independence in effect) in matter and form and accident, and the third (independence in both) in the soul.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents the first rational proof (al-wajh al-awwal) for the intellect's existence as the first creation. The argument is based on the principle that from the truly One (God) only one thing can proceed directly. The author then examines candidates for that first emanation: body, matter and form, one of the two parts of a body, accident, and soul. Each is ruled out because it does not meet the criteria of being one and independent in both existence and effect. A body is composite, so it would introduce multiplicity and its parts would precede it. One part of a body cannot exist independently. An accident requires a subject. A soul requires a body for its actions. Therefore, only the intellect fits: it is simple, self-subsistent, and independent in its activity. The summary reiterates: the first created must be one, independent in existence and effect; only the intellect satisfies this.

Key Terms
الصادر الأول
واحد حقيقي
الجسم
الهيولى والصورة
العرض
النفس
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the first creation could be a body or a soul.
Correction: The proof shows none of these can be the direct product of the One because they are either composite or dependent in existence or effect.

Checkpoint
Why cannot the first emanation from God be a body according to this proof?
A) Because a body is associated with the material world
B) Because a body is composite, which would imply multiplicity from the One
C) Because a body is not self-subsistent
D) Because a body is not eternal

Key Takeaway
The first emanation must be simple and independent; only the intellect satisfies both conditions.
